the secret GARDEN 




 CHAPTER I 

 there be no ONE LEFT 

 when Mary Lennox be send to Misselthwaite Manor to live with her uncle everybody say she be the most disagreeable - look child ever see . it be true , too . she have a little thin face and a little thin body , thin light hair and a sour expression . her hair be yellow , and her face be yellow because she have be bear in India and have always be ill in one way or another . her father have hold a position under the English Government and have always be busy and ill himself , and her mother have be a great beauty who care only to go to party and amuse herself with gay people . she have not want a little girl at all , and when Mary be bear she hand she over to the care of an Ayah , who be make to understand that if she wish to please the Mem Sahib she must keep the child out of sight as much as possible . so when she be a sickly , fretful , ugly little baby she be keep out of the way , and when she become a sickly , fretful , toddle thing she be keep out of the way also . she never remember see familiarly anything but the dark face of her Ayah and the other native servant , and as they always obey she and give she her own way in everything , because the Mem Sahib would be angry if she be disturb by her crying , by the time she be six year old she be as tyrannical and selfish a little pig as ever live . the young english governess who come to teach she to read and write dislike she so much that she give up her place in three month , and when other governess come to try to fill it they always go away in a short time than the first one . so if Mary have not choose to really want to know how to read book she would never have learn her letter at all . 

 one frightfully hot morning , when she be about nine year old , she awaken feel very cross , and she become crosser still when she see that the servant who stand by her bedside be not her ayah . 

 " why do you come ? " she say to the strange woman . " I will not let you stay . send my Ayah to I . " 

 the woman look frightened , but she only stammer that the Ayah could not come and when Mary throw herself into a passion and beat and kick she , she look only more frightened and repeat that it be not possible for the Ayah to come to Missie Sahib . 

 there be something mysterious in the air that morning . nothing be do in its regular order and several of the native servant seem missing , while those whom Mary see slunk or hurry about with ashy and scared face . but no one would tell she anything and her Ayah do not come . she be actually leave alone as the morning go on , and at last she wander out into the garden and begin to play by herself under a tree near the veranda . she pretend that she be make a flower - bed , and she stick big scarlet hibiscus blossom into little heap of earth , all the time grow more and more angry and mutter to herself the thing she would say and the name she would call Saidie when she return . 

 " Pig ! Pig ! daughter of Pigs ! " she say , because to call a native a pig be the bad insult of all . 

 she be grind her tooth and say this over and over again when she hear her mother come out on the veranda with some one . she be with a fair young man and they stand talk together in low strange voice . Mary know the fair young man who look like a boy . she have hear that he be a very young officer who have just come from England . the child star at he , but she star most at her mother . she always do this when she have a chance to see she , because the Mem Sahib Mary use to call she that oftener than anything else be such a tall , slim , pretty person and wear such lovely clothe . her hair be like curly silk and she have a delicate little nose which seem to be disdain thing , and she have large laugh eye . all her clothe be thin and floating , and Mary say they be " full of lace . " they look full of lace than ever this morning , but her eye be not laugh at all . they be large and scared and lift imploringly to the fair boy officer 's face . 

 " be it so very bad ? oh , be it ? " Mary hear she say . 

 " awfully , " the young man answer in a trembling voice . " awfully , Mrs. Lennox . you ought to have go to the hill two week ago . " 

 the Mem Sahib wring her hand . 

 " oh , I know I ought ! " she cry . " I only stay to go to that silly dinner party . what a fool I be ! " 

 at that very moment such a loud sound of wailing break out from the servant ' quarter that she clutch the young man 's arm , and Mary stand shiver from head to foot . the wail grow wilder and wilder . " what be it ? what be it ? " Mrs. Lennox gasp . 

 " some one have die , " answer the boy officer . " you do not say it have break out among your servant . " 

 " I do not know ! " the Mem Sahib cry . " come with I ! come with I ! " and she turn and run into the house . 

 after that , appal thing happen , and the mysteriousness of the morning be explain to Mary . the cholera have break out in its most fatal form and people be die like fly . the Ayah have be take ill in the night , and it be because she have just die that the servant have wail in the hut . before the next day three other servant be dead and other have run away in terror . there be panic on every side , and die people in all the bungalow . 

 during the confusion and bewilderment of the second day Mary hide herself in the nursery and be forget by everyone . nobody think of she , nobody want she , and strange thing happen of which she know nothing . Mary alternately cry and sleep through the hour . she only know that people be ill and that she hear mysterious and frightening sound . once she creep into the dining - room and find it empty , though a partly finish meal be on the table and chair and plate look as if they have be hastily push back when the diner rise suddenly for some reason . the child eat some fruit and biscuit , and be thirsty she drink a glass of wine which stand nearly fill . it be sweet , and she do not know how strong it be . very soon it make she intensely drowsy , and she go back to her nursery and shut herself in again , frighten by cry she hear in the hut and by the hurrying sound of foot . the wine make she so sleepy that she could scarcely keep her eye open and she lie down on her bed and know nothing more for a long time . 

 many thing happen during the hour in which she sleep so heavily , but she be not disturb by the wail and the sound of thing be carry in and out of the bungalow . 

 when she awaken she lie and star at the wall . the house be perfectly still . she have never know it to be so silent before . she hear neither voice nor footstep , and wonder if everybody have get well of the cholera and all the trouble be over . she wonder also who would take care of she now her Ayah be dead . there would be a new ayah , and perhaps she would know some new story . Mary have be rather tired of the old one . she do not cry because her nurse have die . she be not an affectionate child and have never care much for any one . the noise and hurry about and wail over the cholera have frighten she , and she have be angry because no one seem to remember that she be alive . everyone be too panic - stricken to think of a little girl no one be fond of . when people have the cholera it seem that they remember nothing but themselves . but if everyone have get well again , surely some one would remember and come to look for she . 

 but no one come , and as she lie wait the house seem to grow more and more silent . she hear something rustle on the matting and when she look down she see a little snake glide along and watch she with eye like jewel . she be not frightened , because he be a harmless little thing who would not hurt she and he seem in a hurry to get out of the room . he slip under the door as she watch he . 

 " how queer and quiet it be , " she say . " it sound as if there be no one in the bungalow but I and the snake . " 

 almost the next minute she hear footstep in the compound , and then on the veranda . they be man 's footstep , and the man enter the bungalow and talk in low voice . no one go to meet or speak to they and they seem to open door and look into room . " what desolation ! " she hear one voice say . " that pretty , pretty woman ! I suppose the child , too . I hear there be a child , though no one ever see she . " 

 Mary be stand in the middle of the nursery when they open the door a few minute later . she look an ugly , cross little thing and be frown because she be begin to be hungry and feel disgracefully neglect . the first man who come in be a large officer she have once see talk to her father . he look tired and troubled , but when he see she he be so startled that he almost jump back . 

 " Barney ! " he cry out . " there be a child here ! a child alone ! in a place like this ! mercy on we , who be she ! " 

 " I be Mary Lennox , " the little girl say , draw herself up stiffly . she think the man be very rude to call her father 's bungalow " a place like this ! " " I fall asleep when everyone have the cholera and I have only just waken up . why do nobody come ? " 

 " it be the child no one ever see ! " exclaim the man , turn to his companion . " she have actually be forget ! " 

 " why be I forget ? " Mary say , stamp her foot . " why do nobody come ? " 

 the young man whose name be Barney look at her very sadly . Mary even think she see he wink his eye as if to wink tear away . 

 " poor little kid ! " he say . " there be nobody leave to come . " 

 it be in that strange and sudden way that Mary find out that she have neither father nor mother leave ; that they have die and be carry away in the night , and that the few native servant who have not die also have leave the house as quickly as they could get out of it , none of they even remember that there be a Missie Sahib . that be why the place be so quiet . it be true that there be no one in the bungalow but herself and the little rustle snake . 




 CHAPTER II 

 MISTRESS MARY quite CONTRARY 

 Mary have like to look at her mother from a distance and she have think she very pretty , but as she know very little of she she could scarcely have be expect to love she or to miss she very much when she be go . she do not miss she at all , in fact , and as she be a self - absorb child she give her entire thought to herself , as she have always do . if she have be old she would no doubt have be very anxious at be leave alone in the world , but she be very young , and as she have always be take care of , she suppose she always would be . what she think be that she would like to know if she be go to nice people , who would be polite to she and give she her own way as her Ayah and the other native servant have do . 

 she know that she be not go to stay at the english clergyman 's house where she be take at first . she do not want to stay . the english clergyman be poor and he have five child nearly all the same age and they wear shabby clothe and be always quarrel and snatch toy from each other . Mary hat their untidy bungalow and be so disagreeable to they that after the first day or two nobody would play with she . by the second day they have give she a nickname which make she furious . 

 it be Basil who think of it first . Basil be a little boy with impudent blue eye and a turn - up nose , and Mary hat he . she be play by herself under a tree , just as she have be play the day the cholera break out . she be make heap of earth and path for a garden and Basil come and stand near to watch she . presently he get rather interested and suddenly make a suggestion . 

 " why do not   you put a heap of stone there and pretend it be a rockery ? " he say . " there in the middle , " and he lean over she to point . 

 " go away ! " cry Mary . " I do not   want boy . go away ! " 

 for a moment Basil look angry , and then he begin to tease . he be always tease his sister . he dance round and round she and make face and sing and laugh . 

 " Mistress Mary , quite contrary , 
 how do your garden grow ? 
 with silver bell , and cockle shell , 
 and marigold all in a row . " 
 he sing it until the other child hear and laugh , too ; and the crosser Mary get , the more they sing " Mistress Mary , quite contrary " ; and after that as long as she stay with they they call she " Mistress Mary Quite Contrary " when they speak of she to each other , and often when they speak to she . 

 " you be go to be send home , " Basil say to she , " at the end of the week . and we be glad of it . " 

 " I be glad of it , too , " answer Mary . " where be home ? " 

 " she do not   know where home be ! " say Basil , with seven - year - old scorn . " it be England , of course . our grandmama live there and our sister Mabel be send to her last year . you be not go to your grandmama . you have none . you be go to your uncle . his name be Mr. Archibald Craven . " 

 " I do not   know anything about he , " snap Mary . 

 " I know you do not , " Basil answer . " you do not   know anything . girl never do . I hear father and mother talk about he . he live in a great , big , desolate old house in the country and no one go near he . he be so cross he will not   let they , and they would not   come if he would let they . he be a hunchback , and he be horrid . " " I do not   believe you , " say Mary ; and she turn she back and stick her finger in her ear , because she would not listen any more . 

 but she think over it a great deal afterward ; and when Mrs. Crawford tell she that night that she be go to sail away to England in a few day and go to her uncle , Mr. Archibald Craven , who live at Misselthwaite Manor , she look so stony and stubbornly uninterested that they do not know what to think about she . they try to be kind to she , but she only turn she face away when Mrs. Crawford attempt to kiss she , and hold herself stiffly when Mr. Crawford pat her shoulder . 

 " she be such a plain child , " Mrs. Crawford say pityingly , afterward . " and her mother be such a pretty creature . she have a very pretty manner , too , and Mary have the most unattractive way I ever see in a child . the child call she ' mistress Mary Quite Contrary , ' and though it be naughty of they , one can not   help understand it . " 

 " perhaps if her mother have carry she pretty face and her pretty manner oftener into the nursery Mary might have learn some pretty way too . it be very sad , now the poor beautiful thing be go , to remember that many people never even know that she have a child at all . " 

 " I believe she scarcely ever look at she , " sigh Mrs. Crawford . " when her Ayah be dead there be no one to give a thought to the little thing . think of the servant run away and leave she all alone in that desert bungalow . Colonel McGrew say he nearly jump out of his skin when he open the door and find she stand by herself in the middle of the room . " 

 Mary make the long voyage to England under the care of an officer 's wife , who be take her child to leave they in a boarding - school . she be very much absorb in her own little boy and girl , and be rather glad to hand the child over to the woman Mr. Archibald Craven send to meet she , in London . the woman be his housekeeper at Misselthwaite Manor , and her name be Mrs. Medlock . she be a stout woman , with very red cheek and sharp black eye . she wear a very purple dress , a black silk mantle with jet fringe on it and a black bonnet with purple velvet flower which stick up and tremble when she move her head . Mary do not like she at all , but as she very seldom like people there be nothing remarkable in that ; besides which it be very evident Mrs. Medlock do not think much of she . 

 " my word ! she be a plain little piece of good ! " she say . " and we would hear that her mother be a beauty . she have not   hand much of it down , have she , ma'am ? " " perhaps she will improve as she grow old , " the officer 's wife say good - naturedly . " if she be not so sallow and have a nice expression , her feature be rather good . child alter so much . " 

 " she will have to alter a good deal , " answer Mrs. Medlock . " and , there be nothing likely to improve child at Misselthwaite if you ask I ! " they think Mary be not listen because she be stand a little apart from they at the window of the private hotel they have go to . she be watch the pass bus and cab and people , but she hear quite well and be make very curious about her uncle and the place he live in . what sort of a place be it , and what would he be like ? what be a hunchback ? she have never see one . perhaps there be none in India . 

 since she have be live in other people 's house and have have no ayah , she have begin to feel lonely and to think queer thought which be new to she . she have begin to wonder why she have never seem to belong to anyone even when her father and mother have be alive . other child seem to belong to their father and mother , but she have never seem to really be anyone 's little girl . she have have servant , and food and clothe , but no one have take any notice of she . she do not know that this be because she be a disagreeable child ; but then , of course , she do not know she be disagreeable . she often think that other people be , but she do not know that she be so herself . 

 she think Mrs. Medlock the most disagreeable person she have ever see , with her common , highly colored face and her common fine bonnet . when the next day they set out on their journey to Yorkshire , she walk through the station to the railway carriage with her head up and try to keep as far away from she as she could , because she do not want to seem to belong to she . it would have make she angry to think people imagine she be her little girl . 

 but Mrs. Medlock be not in the least disturb by she and her thought . she be the kind of woman who would ' stand no nonsense from young one . " at least , that be what she would have say if she have be ask . she have not want to go to London just when her sister Maria 's daughter be go to be marry , but she have a comfortable , well pay place as housekeeper at Misselthwaite Manor and the only way in which she could keep it be to do at once what Mr. Archibald Craven tell she to do . she never dare even to ask a question . 

 " Captain Lennox and his wife die of the cholera , " Mr. Craven have say in his short , cold way . " Captain Lennox be my wife 's brother and I be their daughter 's guardian . the child be to be bring here . you must go to London and bring she yourself . " 

 so she pack her small trunk and make the journey . 

 Mary sit in her corner of the railway carriage and look plain and fretful . she have nothing to read or to look at , and she have fold her thin little black - glove hand in her lap . her black dress make she look yellower than ever , and her limp light hair straggle from under her black crepe hat . 

 " a more marred - look young one I never see in my life , " Mrs. Medlock think .   Marred be a yorkshire word and mean spoiled and pettish .   she have never see a child who sit so still without do anything ; and at last she get tired of watch she and begin to talk in a brisk , hard voice . 

 " I suppose I may as well tell you something about where you be go to , " she say . " do you know anything about your uncle ? " 

 " no , " say Mary . 

 " never hear your father and mother talk about he ? " 

 " no , " say Mary frown . she frown because she remember that her father and mother have never talk to she about anything in particular . certainly they have never tell her thing . 

 " Humph , " mutter Mrs. Medlock , star at her queer , unresponsive little face . she do not say any more for a few moment and then she begin again . 

 " I suppose you might as well be tell something to prepare you . you be go to a queer place . " 

 Mary say nothing at all , and Mrs. Medlock look rather discomfited by her apparent indifference , but , after take a breath , she go on . 

 " not but that it be a grand big place in a gloomy way , and Mr. Craven be proud of it in his way and that be gloomy enough , too . the house be six hundred year old and it be on the edge of the moor , and there be near a hundred room in it , though most of they 's shut up and lock . and there be picture and fine old furniture and thing that be be there for age , and there be a big park round it and garden and tree with branch trail to the ground some of they . " she pause and take another breath . " but there be nothing else , " she end suddenly . 

 Mary have begin to listen in spite of herself . it all sound so unlike India , and anything new rather attract she . but she do not intend to look as if she be interested . that be one of her unhappy , disagreeable way . so she sit still . 

 " well , " say Mrs. Medlock . " what do you think of it ? " 

 " nothing , " she answer . " I know nothing about such place . " 

 that make Mrs. Medlock laugh a short sort of laugh . 

 " eh ! " she say , " but you be like an old woman . do not   you care ? " 

 " it do not   matter " say Mary , " whether I care or not . " 

 " you be right enough there , " say Mrs. Medlock . " it do not . what you be to be keep at Misselthwaite Manor for I do not   know , unless because it be the easy way . he be not go to trouble himself about you , that be sure and certain . he never trouble himself about no one . " 

 she stop herself as if she have just remember something in time . 

 " he be get a crooked back , " she say . " that set he wrong . he be a sour young man and get no good of all his money and big place till he be marry . " 

 Mary 's eye turn toward she in spite of her intention not to seem to care . she have never think of the hunchback 's be marry and she be a trifle surprised . Mrs. Medlock see this , and as she be a talkative woman she continue with more interest . this be one way of pass some of the time , at any rate . 

 " she be a sweet , pretty thing and he would have walk the world over to get she a blade o ' grass she want . nobody think she would marry he , but she do , and people say she marry he for his money . but she do not   she do not , " positively . " when she die " 

 Mary give a little involuntary jump . 

 " oh ! do she die ! " she exclaim , quite without meaning to . she have just remember a french fairy story she have once read call " Riquet a la Houppe . " it have be about a poor hunchback and a beautiful princess and it have make she suddenly sorry for Mr. Archibald Craven . 

 " yes , she die , " Mrs. Medlock answer . " and it make he queerer than ever . he care about nobody . he will not   see people . Most of the time he go away , and when he be at Misselthwaite he shut himself up in the West Wing and will not   let any one but Pitcher see he . Pitcher 's an old fellow , but he take care of he when he be a child and he know his way . " 

 it sound like something in a book and it do not make Mary feel cheerful . a house with a hundred room , nearly all shut up and with their door lock a house on the edge of a moor whatsoever a moor be sound dreary . a man with a crooked back who shut himself up also ! she star out of the window with her lip pinch together , and it seem quite natural that the rain should have begin to pour down in gray slanting line and splash and stream down the window - pane . if the pretty wife have be alive she might have make thing cheerful by be something like her own mother and by run in and out and go to party as she have do in frock " full of lace . " but she be not there any more . 

 " you need not   expect to see he , because ten to one you will not , " say Mrs. Medlock . " and you must not   expect that there will be people to talk to you . you will have to play about and look after yourself . you will be tell what room you can go into and what room you be to keep out of . there be garden enough . but when you be in the house do not   go wander and poke about . Mr. Craven will not   have it . " 

 " I shall not want to go poke about , " say sour little Mary and just as suddenly as she have begin to be rather sorry for Mr. Archibald Craven she begin to cease to be sorry and to think he be unpleasant enough to deserve all that have happen to he . 

 and she turn her face toward the stream pane of the window of the railway carriage and gaze out at the gray rain - storm which look as if it would go on forever and ever . she watch it so long and steadily that the grayness grow heavy and heavy before her eye and she fall asleep . 




 CHAPTER III 

 across the moor 

 she sleep a long time , and when she awaken Mrs. Medlock have buy a lunchbasket at one of the station and they have some chicken and cold beef and bread and butter and some hot tea . the rain seem to be stream down more heavily than ever and everybody in the station wear wet and glisten waterproof . the guard light the lamp in the carriage , and Mrs. Medlock cheer up very much over her tea and chicken and beef . she eat a great deal and afterward fall asleep herself , and Mary sit and star at she and watch her fine bonnet slip on one side until she herself fall asleep once more in the corner of the carriage , lull by the splashing of the rain against the window . it be quite dark when she awaken again . the train have stop at a station and Mrs. Medlock be shake she . 

 " you have have a sleep ! " she say . " it be time to open your eye ! we be at Thwaite Station and we have   get a long drive before we . " 

 Mary stand up and try to keep her eye open while Mrs. Medlock collect her parcel . the little girl do not offer to help she , because in India native servant always pick up or carry thing and it seem quite proper that other people should wait on one . 

 the station be a small one and nobody but themselves seem to be get out of the train . the station - master speak to Mrs. Medlock in a rough , good - natured way , pronounce his word in a queer broad fashion which Mary find out afterward be Yorkshire . 

 " I see tha 's get back , " he say . " an ' tha 's browt th ' young ' un with thee . " 

 " Aye , that be she , " answer Mrs. Medlock , speak with a Yorkshire accent herself and jerk her head over her shoulder toward Mary . " how be thy Missus ? " 

 " well enow . Th ' carriage be waitin ' outside for thee . " 

 a brougham stand on the road before the little outside platform . Mary see that it be a smart carriage and that it be a smart footman who help she in . his long waterproof coat and the waterproof cover of his hat be shin and dripping with rain as everything be , the burly station - master include . 

 when he shut the door , mount the box with the coachman , and they drive off , the little girl find herself seat in a comfortably cushion corner , but she be not inclined to go to sleep again . she sit and look out of the window , curious to see something of the road over which she be be drive to the queer place Mrs. Medlock have speak of . she be not at all a timid child and she be not exactly frightened , but she feel that there be no knowing what might happen in a house with a hundred room nearly all shut up a house stand on the edge of a moor . 

 " what be a moor ? " she say suddenly to Mrs. Medlock . 

 " look out of the window in about ten minute and you will see , " the woman answer . " we have   get to drive five mile across Missel Moor before we get to the Manor . you will not   see much because it be a dark night , but you can see something . " 

 Mary ask no more question but wait in the darkness of her corner , keep her eye on the window . the carriage lamp cast ray of light a little distance ahead of they and she catch glimpse of the thing they pass . after they have leave the station they have drive through a tiny village and she have see whitewash cottage and the light of a public house . then they have pass a church and a vicarage and a little shop - window or so in a cottage with toy and sweet and odd thing set out for sale . then they be on the highroad and she see hedge and tree . after that there seem nothing different for a long time or at least it seem a long time to she . 

 at last the horse begin to go more slowly , as if they be climb up - hill , and presently there seem to be no more hedge and no more tree . she could see nothing , in fact , but a dense darkness on either side . she lean forward and press her face against the window just as the carriage give a big jolt . 

 " eh ! we be on the moor now sure enough , " say Mrs. Medlock . 

 the carriage lamp shed a yellow light on a rough - look road which seem to be cut through bush and low - grow thing which end in the great expanse of dark apparently spread out before and around they . a wind be rise and make a singular , wild , low , rush sound . 

 " it be it be not the sea , be it ? " say Mary , look round at her companion . 

 " no , not it , " answer Mrs. Medlock . " nor it be not   field nor mountain , it be just mile and mile and mile of wild land that nothing grow on but heather and gorse and broom , and nothing live on but wild pony and sheep . " 

 " I feel as if it might be the sea , if there be water on it , " say Mary . " it sound like the sea just now . " 

 " that be the wind blow through the bush , " Mrs. Medlock say . " it be a wild , dreary enough place to my mind , though there be plenty that like it particularly when the heather 's in bloom . " 

 on and on they drive through the darkness , and though the rain stop , the wind rush by and whistle and make strange sound . the road go up and down , and several time the carriage pass over a little bridge beneath which water rush very fast with a great deal of noise . Mary feel as if the drive would never come to an end and that the wide , bleak moor be a wide expanse of black ocean through which she be pass on a strip of dry land . 

 " I do not   like it , " she say to herself . " I do not   like it , " and she pinch her thin lip more tightly together . 

 the horse be climb up a hilly piece of road when she first catch sight of a light . Mrs. Medlock see it as soon as she do and draw a long sigh of relief . 

 " eh , I be glad to see that bit o ' light twinkling , " she exclaim . " it be the light in the lodge window . we shall get a good cup of tea after a bit , at all event . " 

 it be " after a bit , " as she say , for when the carriage pass through the park gate there be still two mile of avenue to drive through and the tree   which nearly meet overhead   make it seem as if they be drive through a long dark vault . 

 they drive out of the vault into a clear space and stop before an immensely long but low - build house which seem to ramble round a stone court . at first Mary think that there be no light at all in the window , but as she get out of the carriage she see that one room in a corner upstairs show a dull glow . 

 the entrance door be a huge one make of massive , curiously shape panel of oak stud with big iron nail and bind with great iron bar . it open into an enormous hall , which be so dimly light that the face in the portrait on the wall and the figure in the suit of armor make Mary feel that she do not want to look at they . as she stand on the stone floor she look a very small , odd little black figure , and she feel as small and lost and odd as she look . 

 a neat , thin old man stand near the manservant who open the door for they . 

 " you be to take she to her room , " he say in a husky voice . " he do not   want to see she . he be go to London in the morning . " 

 " very well , Mr. Pitcher , " Mrs. Medlock answer . " so long as I know what be expect of I , I can manage . " 

 " what be expect of you , Mrs. Medlock , " Mr. Pitcher say , " be that you make sure that he be not disturb and that he do not   see what he do not   want to see . " 

 and then Mary Lennox be lead up a broad staircase and down a long corridor and up a short flight of step and through another corridor and another , until a door open in a wall and she find herself in a room with a fire in it and a supper on a table . 

 Mrs. Medlock say unceremoniously : 

 " well , here you be ! this room and the next be where you will live and you must keep to they . do not   you forget that ! " 

 it be in this way Mistress Mary arrive at Misselthwaite Manor and she have perhaps never feel quite so contrary in all her life . 




 CHAPTER IV 

 MARTHA 

 when she open her eye in the morning it be because a young housemaid have come into her room to light the fire and be kneel on the hearth - rug rake out the cinder noisily . Mary lie and watch she for a few moment and then begin to look about the room . she have never see a room at all like it and think it curious and gloomy . the wall be cover with tapestry with a forest scene embroider on it . there be fantastically dress people under the tree and in the distance there be a glimpse of the turret of a castle . there be hunter and horse and dog and lady . Mary feel as if she be in the forest with they . out of a deep window she could see a great climb stretch of land which seem to have no tree on it , and to look rather like an endless , dull , purplish sea . 

 " what be that ? " she say , point out of the window . 

 Martha , the young housemaid , who have just rise to her foot , look and point also . " that there ? " she say . 

 " yes . " 

 " that be th ' moor , " with a good - natured grin . " do tha ' like it ? " 

 " no , " answer Mary . " I hate it . " 

 " that be because tha'rt not use to it , " Martha say , go back to her hearth . " Tha ' think it be too big an ' bare now . but tha ' will like it . " 

 " do you ? " inquire Mary . 

 " Aye , that I do , " answer Martha , cheerfully polish away at the grate . " I just love it . it be none bare . it be cover wi ' growin ' thing as smell sweet . it be fair lovely in spring an ' summer when th ' gorse an ' broom an ' heather be in flower . it smell o ' honey an ' there be such a lot o ' fresh air an ' th ' sky look so high an ' th ' bee an ' skylark make such a nice noise hummin ' an ' singin ' . eh ! I would not   live away from th ' moor for anythin ' . " 

 Mary listen to she with a grave , puzzled expression . the native servant she have be use to in India be not in the least like this . they be obsequious and servile and do not presume to talk to their master as if they be their equal . they make salaam and call they " protector of the poor " and name of that sort . indian servant be command to do thing , not ask . it be not the custom to say " please " and " thank you " and Mary have always slap her Ayah in the face when she be angry . she wonder a little what this girl would do if one slap she in the face . she be a round , rosy , good - natured - look creature , but she have a sturdy way which make Mistress Mary wonder if she might not even slap back if the person who slap she be only a little girl . 

 " you be a strange servant , " she say from her pillow , rather haughtily . 

 Martha sit up on her heel , with her black - brush in her hand , and laugh , without seem the least out of temper . 

 " eh ! I know that , " she say . " if there be a grand Missus at Misselthwaite I should never have be even one of th ' under house - maid . I might have be let to be scullerymaid but I would never have be let upstairs . I be too common an ' I talk too much Yorkshire . but this be a funny house for all it be so grand . seem like there be neither Master nor Mistress except Mr. Pitcher an ' Mrs. Medlock . Mr. Craven , he will not   be trouble about anythin ' when he be here , an ' he be nearly always away . Mrs. Medlock give I th ' place out o ' kindness . she tell I she could never have do it if Misselthwaite have be like other big house . " " be you go to be my servant ? " Mary ask , still in her imperious little indian way . 

 Martha begin to rub her grate again . 

 " I be Mrs. Medlock 's servant , " she say stoutly . " an ' she be Mr. Craven 's but I be to do the housemaid 's work up here an ' wait on you a bit . but you will not   need much waitin ' on . " 

 " who be go to dress I ? " demand Mary . 

 Martha sit up on her heel again and star . she speak in broad Yorkshire in her amazement . 

 " Canna ' tha ' dress thysen ! " she say . 

 " what do you mean ? I do not   understand your language , " say Mary . 

 " eh ! I forget , " Martha say . " Mrs. Medlock tell I I would have to be careful or you would not   know what I be sayin ' . I mean can not   you put on your own clothe ? " 

 " no , " answer Mary , quite indignantly . " I never do in my life . my Ayah dress I , of course . " 

 " well , " say Martha , evidently not in the least aware that she be impudent , " it be time tha ' should learn . tha ' can not begin young . it will do thee good to wait on thysen a bit . my mother always say she could not   see why grand people 's child do not   turn out fair fool what with nurse an ' bein ' wash an ' dress an ' take out to walk as if they be puppy ! " 

 " it be different in India , " say Mistress Mary disdainfully . she could scarcely stand this . 

 but Martha be not at all crush . 

 " eh ! I can see it be different , " she answer almost sympathetically . " I dare say it be because there be such a lot o ' black there instead o ' respectable white people . when I hear you be comin ' from India I think you be a black too . " 

 Mary sit up in bed furious . 

 " what ! " she say . " what ! you think I be a native . you you daughter of a pig ! " 

 Martha star and look hot . 

 " who be you callin ' name ? " she say . " you need not   be so vexed . that be not th ' way for a young lady to talk . I have   nothing against th ' black . when you read about them in tract they be always very religious . you always read as a black 's a man an ' a brother . I have   never see a black an ' I be fair pleased to think I be go to see one close . when I come in to light your fire this mornin ' I crep ' up to your bed an ' pull th ' cover back careful to look at you . an ' there you be , " disappointedly , " no more black than I for all you be so yeller . " 

 Mary do not even try to control her rage and humiliation . " you think I be a native ! you dare ! you do not   know anything about native ! they be not people they be servant who must salaam to you . you know nothing about India . you know nothing about anything ! " 

 she be in such a rage and feel so helpless before the girl 's simple stare , and somehow she suddenly feel so horribly lonely and far away from everything she understand and which understand she , that she throw herself face downward on the pillow and burst into passionate sobbing . she sob so unrestrainedly that good - natured Yorkshire Martha be a little frightened and quite sorry for she . she go to the bed and bend over she . 

 " eh ! you must not   cry like that there ! " she beg . " you must not   for sure . I do not   know you would be vex . I do not   know anythin ' about anythin ' just like you say . I beg your pardon , Miss. do stop cryin ' . " 

 there be something comforting and really friendly in her queer Yorkshire speech and sturdy way which have a good effect on Mary . she gradually cease cry and become quiet . Martha look relieve . 

 " it be time for thee to get up now , " she say . " Mrs. Medlock say I be to carry tha ' breakfast an ' tea an ' dinner into th ' room next to this . it be be make into a nursery for thee . I will help thee on with thy clothe if tha'll get out o ' bed . if th ' button be at th ' back tha ' can not button they up tha'self . " 

 when Mary at last decide to get up , the clothe Martha take from the wardrobe be not the one she have wear when she arrive the night before with Mrs. Medlock . 

 " those be not mine , " she say . " mine be black . " 

 she look the thick white wool coat and dress over , and add with cool approval : 

 " those be nice than mine . " 

 " these be th ' one tha ' must put on , " Martha answer . " Mr. Craven order Mrs. Medlock to get them in London . he say ' I will not   have a child dress in black wanderin ' about like a lost soul , ' he say . ' it would make the place sad than it be . put color on she . ' Mother she say she know what he mean . mother always know what a body mean . she do not   hold with black hersel ' . " 

 " I hate black thing , " say Mary . 

 the dressing process be one which teach they both something . Martha have " button up " her little sister and brother but she have never see a child who stand still and wait for another person to do thing for she as if she have neither hand nor foot of her own . 

 " why do not   tha ' put on tha ' own shoe ? " she say when Mary quietly hold out her foot . 

 " my Ayah do it , " answer Mary , star . " it be the custom . " 

 she say that very often " it be the custom . " the native servant be always say it . if one tell they to do a thing their ancestor have not do for a thousand year they gaze at one mildly and say , " it be not the custom " and one know that be the end of the matter . 

 it have not be the custom that Mistress Mary should do anything but stand and allow herself to be dress like a doll , but before she be ready for breakfast she begin to suspect that her life at Misselthwaite Manor would end by teach she a number of thing quite new to her thing such as put on her own shoe and stocking , and pick up thing she let fall . if Martha have be a well - train fine young lady 's maid she would have be more subservient and respectful and would have know that it be her business to brush hair , and button boot , and pick thing up and lie they away . she be , however , only an untrained Yorkshire rustic who have be bring up in a moorland cottage with a swarm of little brother and sister who have never dream of do anything but wait on themselves and on the young one who be either baby in arm or just learn to totter about and tumble over thing . 

 if Mary Lennox have be a child who be ready to be amuse she would perhaps have laugh at Martha 's readiness to talk , but Mary only listen to she coldly and wonder at her freedom of manner . at first she be not at all interested , but gradually , as the girl rattle on in her good - temper , homely way , Mary begin to notice what she be say . 

 " eh ! you should see them all , " she say . " there be twelve of we an ' my father only get sixteen shilling a week . I can tell you my mother 's put to it to get porridge for them all . they tumble about on th ' moor an ' play there all day an ' mother say th ' air of th ' moor fatten them . she say she believe they eat th ' grass same as th ' wild pony do . our Dickon , he be twelve year old and he be get a young pony he call his own . " 

 " where do he get it ? " ask Mary . 

 " he find it on th ' moor with its mother when it be a little one an ' he begin to make friend with it an ' give it bit o ' bread an ' pluck young grass for it . and it get to like he so it follow he about an ' it let he get on its back . Dickon 's a kind lad an ' animal like he . " 

 Mary have never possess an animal pet of her own and have always think she should like one . so she begin to feel a slight interest in Dickon , and as she have never before be interested in any one but herself , it be the dawning of a healthy sentiment . when she go into the room which have be make into a nursery for she , she find that it be rather like the one she have sleep in . it be not a child 's room , but a grow - up person 's room , with gloomy old picture on the wall and heavy old oak chair . a table in the center be set with a good substantial breakfast . but she have always have a very small appetite , and she look with something more than indifference at the first plate Martha set before she . 

 " I do not   want it , " she say . 

 " Tha ' do not   want thy porridge ! " Martha exclaim incredulously . 

 " no . " 

 " Tha ' do not   know how good it be . put a bit o ' treacle on it or a bit o ' sugar . " 

 " I do not   want it , " repeat Mary . 

 " eh ! " say Martha . " I can not   abide to see good victual go to waste . if our child be at this table they would clean it bare in five minute . " 

 " why ? " say Mary coldly . " why ! " echo Martha . " because they scarce ever have their stomach full in their life . they be as hungry as young hawk an ' fox . " 

 " I do not   know what it be to be hungry , " say Mary , with the indifference of ignorance . 

 Martha look indignant . 

 " well , it would do thee good to try it . I can see that plain enough , " she say outspokenly . " I have   no patience with folk as sit an ' just stare at good bread an ' meat . my word ! do not   I wish Dickon and Phil an ' Jane an ' th ' rest of them have what be here under their pinafore . " 

 " why do not   you take it to they ? " suggest Mary . 

 " it be not mine , " answer Martha stoutly . " an ' this be not   my day out . I get my day out once a month same as th ' rest . then I go home an ' clean up for mother an ' give she a day 's rest . " 

 Mary drink some tea and eat a little toast and some marmalade . 

 " you wrap up warm an ' run out an ' play you , " say Martha . " it will do you good and give you some stomach for your meat . " 

 Mary go to the window . there be garden and path and big tree , but everything look dull and wintry . 

 " out ? why should I go out on a day like this ? " " well , if tha ' do not   go out tha'lt have to stay in , an ' what have tha ' get to do ? " 

 Mary glance about she . there be nothing to do . when Mrs. Medlock have prepare the nursery she have not think of amusement . perhaps it would be well to go and see what the garden be like . 

 " who will go with I ? " she inquire . 

 Martha star . 

 " you will go by yourself , " she answer . " you will have to learn to play like other child do when they have not   get sister and brother . our Dickon go off on th ' moor by himself an ' play for hour . that be how he make friend with th ' pony . he be get sheep on th ' moor that know he , an ' bird as come an ' eat out of his hand . however little there be to eat , he always save a bit o ' his bread to coax his pet . " 

 it be really this mention of Dickon which make Mary decide to go out , though she be not aware of it . there would be , bird outside though there would not be pony or sheep . they would be different from the bird in India and it might amuse she to look at they . 

 Martha find her coat and hat for she and a pair of stout little boot and she show she her way downstairs . 

 " if tha ' go round that way tha'll come to th ' garden , " she say , point to a gate in a wall of shrubbery . " there be lot o ' flower in summer - time , but there be nothing bloomin ' now . " she seem to hesitate a second before she add , " one of th ' garden be lock up . no one have be in it for ten year . " 

 " why ? " ask Mary in spite of herself . here be another locked door add to the hundred in the strange house . 

 " Mr. Craven have it shut when his wife die so sudden . he will not   let no one go inside . it be her garden . he lock th ' door an ' dig a hole and bury th ' key . there be Mrs. Medlock 's bell ring I must run . " 

 after she be go Mary turn down the walk which lead to the door in the shrubbery . she could not help think about the garden which no one have be into for ten year . she wonder what it would look like and whether there be any flower still alive in it . when she have pass through the shrubbery gate she find herself in great garden , with wide lawn and winding walk with clipped border . there be tree , and flower - bed , and evergreen clip into strange shape , and a large pool with an old gray fountain in its midst . but the flower - bed be bare and wintry and the fountain be not play . this be not the garden which be shut up . how could a garden be shut up ? you could always walk into a garden . 

 she be just think this when she see that , at the end of the path she be follow , there seem to be a long wall , with ivy grow over it . she be not familiar enough with England to know that she be come upon the kitchen - garden where the vegetable and fruit be grow . she go toward the wall and find that there be a green door in the ivy , and that it stand open . this be not the closed garden , evidently , and she could go into it .

 presently an old man with a spade over his shoulder walk through the door lead from the second garden . he look startled when he see Mary , and then touch his cap . he have a surly old face , and do not seem at all pleased to see she but then she be displeased with his garden and wear she " quite contrary " expression , and certainly do not seem at all pleased to see he . 

 " what be this place ? " she ask . 

 " one o ' th ' kitchen - garden , " he answer . 

 " what be that ? " say Mary , point through the other green door . 

 " another of them , " shortly . " there be another on t'other side o ' th ' wall an ' there be th ' orchard t'other side o ' that . "

 " if tha ' like . but there be nowt to see . " 

 Mary make no response . she go down the path and through the second green door . there , she find more wall and winter vegetable and glass frame , but in the second wall there be another green door and it be not open . perhaps it lead into the garden which no one have see for ten year . as she be not at all a timid child and always do what she want to do , Mary go to the green door and turn the handle . she hop the door would not open because she want to be sure she have find the mysterious garden but it do open quite easily and she walk through it and find herself in an orchard . there be wall all round it also and tree train against they , and there be bare fruit - tree grow in the winter - brown grass but there be no green door to be see anywhere .  perhaps it be because she have nothing whatever to do that she think so much of the deserted garden . she be curious about it and want to see what it be like . why have Mr. Archibald Craven bury the key ? if he have like his wife so much why do he hate her garden ? she wonder if she should ever see he , but she know that if she do she should not like he , and he would not like she , and that she should only stand and stare at he and say nothing , though she should be want dreadfully to ask he why he have do such a queer thing .

 " I have be into the other garden , " she say . 

 " there be nothing to prevent thee , " he answer crustily . 

 " I go into the orchard . "

 " there be no door there into the other garden , " say Mary . 

 " what garden ? " he say in a rough voice , stop his digging for a moment .

 " here he be , " chuckle the old man , and then he speak to the bird as if he be speak to a child . 

 " where have tha ' be , tha ' cheeky little beggar ? " he say . " I have   not see thee before today . have tha , begin tha ' courtin ' this early in th ' season ? Tha'rt too forrad . " 

 the bird put his tiny head on one side and look up at he with his soft bright eye which be like a black dewdrop . he seem quite familiar and not the least afraid . he hop about and peck the earth briskly , look for seed and insect . it actually give Mary a queer feeling in her heart , because he be so pretty and cheerful and seem so like a person . he have a tiny plump body and a delicate beak , and slender delicate leg . 

 " will he always come when you call he ? " she ask almost in a whisper . 

 " Aye , that he will . I have   know he ever since he be a fledgling . he come out of th ' nest in th ' other garden an ' when first he fly over th ' wall he be too weak to fly back for a few day an ' we get friendly . when he go over th ' wall again th ' rest of th ' brood be go an ' he be lonely an ' he come back to I . " 

 " what kind of a bird be he ? " Mary ask . 

 " do not   tha ' know ? he be a robin redbreast an ' they be th ' friendly , curious bird alive . they be almost as friendly as dog if you know how to get on with them . watch he peckin ' about there an ' lookin ' round at we now an ' again . he know we be talkin ' about he . " 

 it be the queer thing in the world to see the old fellow . he look at the plump little scarlet - waistcoate bird as if he be both proud and fond of he .

" he like to hear folk talk about he . an ' curious bless I , there never be his like for curiosity an ' meddlin ' . he be always comin ' to see what I be plantin ' . he know all th ' thing Mester Craven never trouble hissel ' to find out . he be th ' head gardener , he be . " 

 the robin hop about busily peck the soil and now and then stop and look at they a little . Mary think his black dewdrop eye gaze at she with great curiosity . it really seem as if he be find out all about she . the queer feeling in her heart increase . " where do the rest of the brood fly to ? " she ask . 

 " there be no knowin ' . the old one turn them out o ' their nest an ' make them fly an ' they be scatter before you know it . this one be a knowin ' one an ' he know he be lonely . " 

 Mistress Mary go a step near to the robin and look at he very hard . 

 " I be lonely , " she say . 

 she have not know before that this be one of the thing which make she feel sour and cross . she seem to find it out when the robin look at she and she look at the robin .

 " art tha ' th ' little wench from India ? " he ask . 

 Mary nod . 

 " then no wonder tha'rt lonely . Tha'lt be lonlier before tha 's do , " he say . 

 he begin to dig again , drive his spade deep into the rich black garden soil while the robin hop about very busily employ . 

 " what be your name ? " Mary inquire . 

 he stand up to answer she . 

 " Ben Weatherstaff , " he answer , and then he add with a surly chuckle , " I be lonely mysel ' except when he be with I , " and he jerk his thumb toward the robin . " he be th ' only friend I have   get . " 

 " I have no friend at all , " say Mary . " I never have . my Ayah do not   like I and I never play with any one . " 

 it be a Yorkshire habit to say what you think with blunt frankness , and old Ben Weatherstaff be a Yorkshire moor man . 

 " Tha ' an ' I be a good bit alike , " he say . " we be weave out of th ' same cloth . we be neither of we good lookin ' an ' we be both of we as sour as we look . we have   get the same nasty temper , both of we , I will warrant . " 

 this be plain speak , and Mary Lennox have never hear the truth about herself in her life . native servant always salaam and submit to you , whatever you do . she have never think much about her look , but she wonder if she be as unattractive as Ben Weatherstaff and she also wonder if she look as sour as he have look before the robin come . she actually begin to wonder also if she be " nasty temper . " she feel uncomfortable .

 " what do he do that for ? " ask Mary . 

 " he be make up his mind to make friend with thee , " reply Ben . " dang I if he have not   take a fancy to thee . " 

 " to I ? " say Mary , and she move toward the little tree softly and look up . 

 " would you make friend with I ? " she say to the robin just as if she be speak to a person . " would you ? " and she do not say it either in her hard little voice or in her imperious indian voice , but in a tone so soft and eager and coax that Ben Weatherstaff be as surprised as she have be when she hear he whistle . 

 " why , " he cry out , " tha ' say that as nice an ' human as if tha ' be a real child instead of a sharp old woman . Tha ' say it almost like Dickon talk to his wild thing on th ' moor . " 

 " do you know Dickon ? " Mary ask , turn round rather in a hurry . 

 " everybody know he . Dickon 's wanderin ' about everywhere . th ' very blackberry an ' heather - bell know he . I warrant th ' fox show he where their cub lie an ' th ' skylark do not   hide their nest from he . " 

 Mary would have like to ask some more question . she be almost as curious about Dickon as she be about the deserted garden . but just that moment the robin , who have end his song , give a little shake of his wing , spread they and fly away . he have make his visit and have other thing to do . 

 " he have fly over the wall ! " Mary cry out , watch he . " he have fly into the orchard he have fly across the other wall into the garden where there be no door ! " 

 " he live there , " say old Ben . " he come out o ' th ' egg there . if he be courtin ' , he be makin ' up to some young madam of a robin that live among th ' old rose - tree there . " 

 " rose - tree , " say Mary . " be there rise - tree ? " 

 Ben Weatherstaff take up his spade again and begin to dig . 

 " there be ten year ' ago , " he mumble . 

 " I should like to see they , " say Mary . " where be the green door ? there must be a door somewhere . " 

 Ben drive his spade deep and look as uncompanionable as he have look when she first see he . 

 " there be ten year ' ago , but there be not   now , " he say . 

 " no door ! " cry Mary . " there must be . " " none as any one can find , an ' none as be any one 's business . do not   you be a meddlesome wench an ' poke your nose where it be no cause to go . here , I must go on with my work . get you go an ' play you . I have   no more time . " 

 and he actually stop dig , throw his spade over his shoulder and walk off , without even glance at she or say good - by . 




 CHAPTER V 

 the CRY in the corridor 

 at first each day which pass by for Mary Lennox be exactly like the other . every morning she awake in her tapestried room and find Martha kneeling upon the hearth build her fire ; every morning she eat her breakfast in the nursery which have nothing amusing in it ; and after each breakfast she gaze out of the window across to the huge moor which seem to spread out on all side and climb up to the sky , and after she have star for a while she realize that if she do not go out she would have to stay in and do nothing and so she go out . she do not know that this be the good thing she could have do , and she do not know that , when she begin to walk quickly or even run along the path and down the avenue , she be stir her slow blood and make herself strong by fight with the wind which sweep down from the moor . she run only to make herself warm , and she hat the wind which rush at her face and roar and hold she back as if it be some giant she could not see . but the big breath of rough fresh air blow over the heather fill her lung with something which be good for her whole thin body and whip some red color into her cheek and brighten her dull eye when she do not know anything about it . 

 but after a few day spend almost entirely out of door she waken one morning know what it be to be hungry , and when she sit down to her breakfast she do not glance disdainfully at her porridge and push it away , but take up her spoon and begin to eat it and go on eat it until her bowl be empty . 

 " Tha ' get on well enough with that this mornin ' , do not   tha ' ? " say Martha . 

 " it taste nice today , " say Mary , feel a little surprised her self . 

 " it be th ' air of th ' moor that be givin ' thee stomach for tha ' victual , " answer Martha . " it be lucky for thee that tha 's get victual as well as appetite . there be be twelve in our cottage as have th ' stomach an ' nothing to put in it . you go on playin ' you out o ' door every day an ' you will get some flesh on your bone an ' you will not   be so yell . " 

 " I do not   play , " say Mary . " I have nothing to play with . " 

 " nothing to play with ! " exclaim Martha . " our child play with stick and stone . they just run about an ' shout an ' look at thing . " Mary do not shout , but she look at thing . there be nothing else to do . she walk round and round the garden and wander about the path in the park . sometimes she look for Ben Weatherstaff , but though several time she see he at work he be too busy to look at she or be too surly . once when she be walk toward he he pick up his spade and turn away as if he do it on purpose . 

 one place she go to oftener than to any other . it be the long walk outside the garden with the wall round they . there be bare flower - bed on either side of it and against the wall ivy grow thickly . there be one part of the wall where the creep dark green leaf be more bushy than elsewhere . it seem as if for a long time that part have be neglect . the rest of it have be clip and make to look neat , but at this low end of the walk it have not be trim at all . 

 a few day after she have talk to Ben Weatherstaff , Mary stop to notice this and wonder why it be so . she have just pause and be look up at a long spray of ivy swing in the wind when she see a gleam of scarlet and hear a brilliant chirp , and there , on the top of the wall , forward perch Ben Weatherstaff 's robin redbreast , tilt forward to look at she with his small head on one side . 

 " oh ! " she cry out , " be it you be it you ? " and it do not seem at all queer to she that she speak to he as if she be sure that he would understand and answer she . 

 he do answer . he twitter and chirp and hop along the wall as if he be tell she all sort of thing . it seem to mistress Mary as if she understand he , too , though he be not speak in word . it be as if he say : 

 " good morning ! be not   the wind nice ? be not   the sun nice ? be not   everything nice ? let we both chirp and hop and twitter . come on ! come on ! " 

 Mary begin to laugh , and as he hop and take little flight along the wall she run after he . poor little thin , sallow , ugly Mary she actually look almost pretty for a moment . 

 " I like you ! I like you ! " she cry out , patter down the walk ; and she chirp and try to whistle , which last she do not know how to do in the least . but the robin seem to be quite satisfied and chirp and whistle back at she . at last he spread his wing and make a dart flight to the top of a tree , where he perch and sing loudly . that remind Mary of the first time she have see he . he have be swing on a tree - top then and she have be stand in the orchard . now she be on the other side of the orchard and stand in the path outside a wall much lower down and there be the same tree inside . 

 " it be in the garden no one can go into , " she say to herself . " it be the garden without a door . he live in there . how I wish I could see what it be like ! " 

 she run up the walk to the green door she have enter the first morning . then she run down the path through the other door and then into the orchard , and when she stand and look up there be the tree on the other side of the wall , and there be the robin just finish his song and , begin to preen his feather with his beak . 

 " it be the garden , " she say . " I be sure it be . " 

 she walk round and look closely at that side of the orchard wall , but she only find what she have find before that there be no door in it . then she run through the kitchen - garden again and out into the walk outside the long ivy - cover wall , and she walk to the end of it and look at it , but there be no door ; and then she walk to the other end , look again , but there be no door . 

 " it be very queer , " she say . " Ben Weatherstaff say there be no door and there be no door . but there must have be one ten year ago , because Mr. Craven bury the key . " 

 this give she so much to think of that she begin to be quite interested and feel that she be not sorry that she have come to Misselthwaite Manor . in India she have always feel hot and too languid to care much about anything . the fact be that the fresh wind from the moor have begin to blow the cobwebs out of her young brain and to waken she up a little . 

 she stay out of door nearly all day , and when she sit down to her supper at night she feel hungry and drowsy and comfortable . she do not feel cross when Martha chatter away . she feel as if she rather like to hear she , and at last she think she would ask she a question . she ask it after she have finish her supper and have sit down on the hearth - rug before the fire . 

 " why do Mr. Craven hate the garden ? " she say . 

 she have make Martha stay with she and Martha have not object at all . she be very young , and use to a crowded cottage full of brother and sister , and she find it dull in the great servant ' hall downstairs where the footman and upper - housemaid make fun of her Yorkshire speech and look upon she as a common little thing , and sit and whisper among themselves . Martha like to talk , and the strange child who have live in India , and be wait upon by " black , " be novelty enough to attract she . 

 she sit down on the hearth herself without wait to be ask . 

 " art tha ' thinkin ' about that garden yet ? " she say . " I know tha ' would . that be just the way with I when I first hear about it . " 

 " why do he hate it ? " Mary persist . 

 Martha tuck her foot under she and make herself quite comfortable . 

 " listen to th ' wind wutherin ' round the house , " she say . " you could bare stand up on the moor if you be out on it tonight . " 

 Mary do not know what " wutherin ' " mean until she listen , and then she understand . it must mean that hollow shuddering sort of roar which rush round and round the house as if the giant no one could see be buffet it and beat at the wall and window to try to break in . but one know he could not get in , and somehow it make one feel very safe and warm inside a room with a red coal fire . 

 " but why do he hate it so ? " she ask , after she have listen . she intend to know if Martha do . 

 then Martha give up her store of knowledge . 

 " mind , " she say , " Mrs. Medlock say it be not to be talk about . there be lot o ' thing in this place that be not to be talk over . that be Mr. Craven 's order . his trouble be none servant ' business , he say . but for th ' garden he would not   be like he be . it be Mrs. Craven 's garden that she have make when first they be marry an ' she just love it , an ' they use to ' tend the flower themselves . an ' none o ' th ' gardener be ever let to go in . he an ' she use to go in an ' shut th ' door an ' stay there hour an ' hour , readin ' and talkin ' . an ' she be just a bit of a girl an ' there be an old tree with a branch bent like a seat on it . an ' she make rose grow over it an ' she use to sit there . but one day when she be sittin ' there th ' branch break an ' she fall on th ' ground an ' be hurt so bad that next day she die . Th ' doctor think he would go out o ' his mind an ' die , too . that be why he hat it . no one be never go in since , an ' he will not   let any one talk about it . " 

 Mary do not ask any more question . she look at the red fire and listen to the wind " wutherin ' . " it seem to be " wutherin ' " louder than ever . at that moment a very good thing be happen to she . four good thing have happen to she , in fact , since she come to Misselthwaite Manor . she have feel as if she have understand a robin and that he have understand she ; she have run in the wind until her blood have grow warm ; she have be healthily hungry for the first time in her life ; and she have find out what it be to be sorry for some one . 

 but as she be listen to the wind she begin to listen to something else . she do not know what it be , because at first she could scarcely distinguish it from the wind itself . it be a curious sound it seem almost as if a child be cry somewhere . sometimes the wind sound rather like a child crying , but presently Mistress Mary feel quite sure this sound be inside the house , not outside it . it be far away , but it be inside . she turn round and look at Martha . 

 " do you hear any one cry ? " she say . 

 Martha suddenly look confused . 

 " no , " she answer . " it be th ' wind . sometimes it sound like as if some one be lose on th ' moor an ' wailin ' . it be get all sort o ' sound . " 

 " but listen , " say Mary . " it be in the house down one of those long corridor . " 

 and at that very moment a door must have be open somewhere downstairs ; for a great rushing draft blow along the passage and the door of the room they sit in be blow open with a crash , and as they both jump to their foot the light be blow out and the cry sound be sweep down the far corridor so that it be to be hear more plainly than ever . 

 " there ! " say Mary . " I tell you so ! it be some one cry and it be not   a grow - up person . " 

 Martha run and shut the door and turn the key , but before she do it they both hear the sound of a door in some far passage shut with a bang , and then everything be quiet , for even the wind cease " wutherin ' " for a few moment . 

 " it be th ' wind , " say Martha stubbornly . " an ' if it be not , it be little Betty Butterworth , th ' scullery - maid . she be have th ' toothache all day . " 

 but something troubled and awkward in her manner make Mistress Mary stare very hard at she . she do not believe she be speak the truth . 




 CHAPTER VI 

 " THERE be some one crying there be ! " 

 the next day the rain pour down in torrent again , and when Mary look out of her window the moor be almost hide by gray mist and cloud . there could be no go out today . 

 " what do you do in your cottage when it rain like this ? " she ask Martha . 

 " try to keep from under each other 's foot mostly , " Martha answer . " eh ! there do seem a lot of we then . Mother 's a good - temper woman but she get fair moithered . the big one go out in th ' cow - shed and play there . Dickon he do not   mind th ' wet . he go out just th ' same as if th ' sun be shinin ' . he say he see thing on rainy day as do not   show when it be fair weather . he once find a little fox cub half drown in its hole and he bring it home in th ' bosom of his shirt to keep it warm . its mother have be kill nearby an ' th ' hole be swum out an ' th ' rest o ' th ' litter be dead . he be get it at home now . he find a half - drown young crow another time an ' he bring it home , too , an ' tame it . it be name Soot because it be so black , an ' it hop an ' fly about with he everywhere . " 

 the time have come when Mary have forget to resent Martha 's familiar talk . she have even begin to find it interesting and to be sorry when she stop or go away . the story she have be tell by her Ayah when she live in India have be quite unlike those Martha have to tell about the moorland cottage which hold fourteen people who live in four little room and never have quite enough to eat . the child seem to tumble about and amuse themselves like a litter of rough , good - natured collie puppy . Mary be most attract by the mother and Dickon . when Martha tell story of what " mother " say or do they always sound comfortable . 

 " if I have a raven or a fox cub I could play with it , " say Mary . " but I have nothing . " 

 Martha look perplexed . 

 " can tha ' knit ? " she ask . 

 " no , " answer Mary . 

 " can tha ' sew ? " 

 " no . " 

 " can tha ' read ? " 

 " yes . " 

 " then why do not   tha , read something , or learn a bit o ' spellin ' ? tha'st old enough to be learnin ' thy book a good bit now . " 

 " I have not   any book , " say Mary . " those I have be leave in India . " 

 " that be a pity , " say Martha . " if Mrs. Medlock'd let thee go into th ' library , there be thousand o ' book there . " 

 Mary do not ask where the library be , because she be suddenly inspire by a new idea . she make up her mind to go and find it herself . she be not trouble about Mrs. Medlock . Mrs. Medlock seem always to be in her comfortable housekeeper 's sit - room downstair . in this queer place one scarcely ever see any one at all . in fact , there be no one to see but the servant , and when their master be away they live a luxurious life below stair , where there be a huge kitchen hang about with shin brass and pewter , and a large servant ' hall where there be four or five abundant meal eat every day , and where a great deal of lively romping go on when Mrs. Medlock be out of the way . 

 Mary 's meal be serve regularly , and Martha wait on she , but no one trouble themselves about she in the least . Mrs. Medlock come and look at she every day or two , but no one inquire what she do or tell she what to do . she suppose that perhaps this be the english way of treat child . in India she have always be attend by her Ayah , who have follow she about and wait on she , hand and foot . she have often be tired of her company . now she be follow by nobody and be learn to dress herself because Martha look as though she think she be silly and stupid when she want to have thing hand to she and put on . 

 " have not   tha ' get good sense ? " she say once , when Mary have stand wait for she to put on her glove for she . " our Susan Ann be twice as sharp as thee an ' she be only four year ' old . sometimes tha ' look fair soft in th ' head . " 

 Mary have wear her contrary scowl for an hour after that , but it make she think several entirely new thing .

 she open the door of the room and go into the corridor , and then she begin her wandering . it be a long corridor and it branch into other corridor and it lead she up short flight of step which mount to other again . there be door and door , and there be picture on the wall . sometimes they be picture of dark , curious landscape , but oftenest they be portrait of man and woman in queer , grand costume make of satin and velvet . she find herself in one long gallery whose wall be cover with these portrait . she have never think there could be so many in any house . she walk slowly down this place and star at the face which also seem to stare at she . she feel as if they be wonder what a little girl from India be do in their house . some be picture of child little girl in thick satin frock which reach to their foot and stand out about they , and boy with puff sleeve and lace collar and long hair , or with big ruff around their neck . she always stop to look at the child , and wonder what their name be , and where they have go , and why they wear such odd clothe . there be a stiff , plain little girl rather like herself . she wear a green brocade dress and hold a green parrot on her finger . her eye have a sharp , curious look . 

 " where do you live now ? " say Mary aloud to she . " I wish you be here . " 

 surely no other little girl ever spend such a queer morning . it seem as if there be no one in all the huge ramble house but her own small self , wander about upstairs and down , through narrow passage and wide one , where it seem to she that no one but herself have ever walk . since so many room have be build , people must have live in they , but it all seem so empty that she could not quite believe it true . 

 it be not until she climb to the second floor that she think of turn the handle of a door . all the door be shut , as Mrs. Medlock have say they be , but at last she put her hand on the handle of one of they and turn it . she be almost frightened for a moment when she feel that it turn without difficulty and that when she push upon the door itself it slowly and heavily open . it be a massive door and open into a big bedroom . there be embroider hanging on the wall , and inlay furniture such as she have see in India stand about the room . a broad window with leaded pane look out upon the moor ; and over the mantel be another portrait of the stiff , plain little girl who seem to stare at she more curiously than ever . 

 " perhaps she sleep here once , " say Mary . " she star at I so that she make I feel queer . " 

 after that she open more door and more . she see so many room that she become quite tired and begin to think that there must be a hundred , though she have not count they . in all of they there be old picture or old tapestry with strange scene work on they . there be curious piece of furniture and curious ornament in nearly all of they . 

 in one room , which look like a lady 's sitting - room , the hanging be all embroider velvet , and in a cabinet be about a hundred little elephant make of ivory . they be of different size , and some have their mahout or palanquin on their back . some be much big than the other and some be so tiny that they seem only baby . Mary have see carve ivory in India and she know all about elephant . she open the door of the cabinet and stand on a footstool and play with these for quite a long time . when she get tired she set the elephant in order and shut the door of the cabinet . 

 in all her wandering through the long corridor and the empty room , she have see nothing alive ; but in this room she see something . just after she have close the cabinet door she hear a tiny rustle sound . it make her jump and look around at the sofa by the fireplace , from which it seem to come . in the corner of the sofa there be a cushion , and in the velvet which cover it there be a hole , and out of the hole peep a tiny head with a pair of frightened eye in it . 

 Mary creep softly across the room to look . the bright eye belong to a little gray mouse , and the mouse have eat a hole into the cushion and make a comfortable nest there . six baby mouse be cuddle up asleep near she . if there be no one else alive in the hundred room there be seven mouse who do not look lonely at all . 

 " if they would not   be so frightened I would take they back with I , " say Mary . 

 she have wander about long enough to feel too tired to wander any far , and she turn back . two or three time she lose her way by turn down the wrong corridor and be oblige to ramble up and down until she find the right one ; but at last she reach her own floor again , though she be some distance from her own room and do not know exactly where she be . 

 " I believe I have take a wrong turning again , " she say , stand still at what seem the end of a short passage with tapestry on the wall . " I do not   know which way to go . how still everything be ! "

 " it be near than it be , " say Mary , her heart beat rather fast . " and it be cry . " 

 she put her hand accidentally upon the tapestry near she , and then spring back , feel quite startled . the tapestry be the covering of a door which fall open and show she that there be another part of the corridor behind it , and Mrs. Medlock be come up it with her bunch of key in her hand and a very cross look on her face . 

 " what be you do here ? " she say , and she take Mary by the arm and pull she away . " what do I tell you ? " 

 " I turn round the wrong corner , " explain Mary . " I do not   know which way to go and I hear some one cry . " she quite hat Mrs. Medlock at the moment , but she hat she more the next . 

 " you do not   hear anything of the sort , " say the housekeeper . " you come along back to your own nursery or I will box your ear . " 

 and she take she by the arm and half push , half pull she up one passage and down another until she push she in at the door of her own room . 

 " now , " she say , " you stay where you be tell to stay or you will find yourself lock up . the master have well get you a governess , same as he say he would . you be one that need some one to look sharp after you . I have   get enough to do . "
