 " there be some one cry there be there be ! " she say to herself . 

 she have hear it twice now , and sometime she would find out . she have find out a great deal this morning . she feel as if she have be on a long journey , and at any rate she have have something to amuse she all the time , and she have play with the ivory elephant and have see the gray mouse and its baby in their nest in the velvet cushion . 




 CHAPTER VII 

 the key to the GARDEN 

 two day after this , when Mary open her eye she sit upright in bed immediately , and call to Martha . 

 " look at the moor ! look at the moor ! " 

 the rainstorm have end and the gray mist and cloud have be sweep away in the night by the wind . the wind itself have cease and a brilliant , deep blue sky arch high over the moorland . never , never have Mary dream of a sky so blue . in India sky be hot and blazing ; this be of a deep cool blue which almost seem to sparkle like the water of some lovely bottomless lake , and here and there , high , high in the arched blueness float small cloud of snow - white fleece . the far - reach world of the moor itself look softly blue instead of gloomy purple - black or awful dreary gray . 

 " Aye , " say Martha with a cheerful grin . " Th ' storm be over for a bit . it do like this at this time o ' th ' year . it go off in a night like it be pretendin ' it have never be here an ' never mean to come again . that be because th ' springtime be on its way . it be a long way off yet , but it be comin ' . " 

 " I think perhaps it always rain or look dark in England , " Mary say . 

 " eh ! no ! " say Martha , sit up on her heel among her black lead brush . " nowt o ' th ' soart ! " 

 " what do that mean ? " ask Mary seriously . in India the native speak different dialect which only a few people understand , so she be not surprised when Martha use word she do not know . 

 Martha laugh as she have do the first morning . 

 " there now , " she say . " I have   talk broad Yorkshire again like Mrs. Medlock say I must not . ' nowt o ' th ' soart ' mean ' nothin'-of - the - sort , ' " slowly and carefully , " but it take so long to say it . Yorkshire 's th ' sunniest place on earth when it be sunny . I tell thee tha'd like th ' moor after a bit . just you wait till you see th ' gold - color gorse blossom an ' th ' blossom o ' th ' broom , an ' th ' heather flowerin ' , all purple bell , an ' hundred o ' butterfly flutterin ' an ' bee hummin ' an ' skylark soarin ' up an ' singin ' . you will want to get out on it as sunrise an ' live out on it all day like Dickon do . " " could I ever get there ? " ask Mary wistfully , look through her window at the far - off blue . it be so new and big and wonderful and such a heavenly color . 

 " I do not   know , " answer Martha . " Tha 's never use tha ' leg since tha ' be bear , it seem to I . Tha ' could not   walk five mile . it be five mile to our cottage . " 

 " I should like to see your cottage . " 

 Martha star at she a moment curiously before she take up her polishing brush and begin to rub the grate again . she be think that the small plain face do not look quite as sour at this moment as it have do the first morning she see it . it look just a trifle like little Susan Ann 's when she want something very much . 

 " I will ask my mother about it , " she say . " she be one o ' they that nearly always see a way to do thing . it be my day out today an ' I be go home . eh ! I be glad . Mrs. Medlock think a lot o ' mother . perhaps she could talk to she . " 

 " I like your mother , " say Mary . 

 " I should think tha ' do , " agree Martha , polish away . 

 " I have   never see she , " say Mary . 

 " no , tha ' have not , " reply Martha . 

 she sit up on her heel again and rub the end of her nose with the back of her hand as if puzzle for a moment , but she end quite positively . 

 " well , she be that sensible an ' hard workin ' an ' goodnatured an ' clean that no one could help likin ' she whether they would see she or not . when I be go home to she on my day out I just jump for joy when I be crossin ' the moor . " 

 " I like Dickon , " add Mary . " and I have   never see he . " 

 " well , " say Martha stoutly , " I have   tell thee that th ' very bird like he an ' th ' rabbit an ' wild sheep an ' pony , an ' th ' fox themselves . I wonder , " star at she reflectively , " what Dickon would think of thee ? " 

 " he would not   like I , " say Mary in her stiff , cold little way . " no one do . " 

 Martha look reflective again . 

 " how do tha ' like thysel ' ? " she inquire , really quite as if she be curious to know . 

 Mary hesitate a moment and think it over . 

 " not at all really , " she answer . " but I never think of that before . " 

 Martha grin a little as if at some homely recollection . 

 " Mother say that to I once , " she say . " she be at her wash - tub an ' I be in a bad temper an ' talkin ' ill of folk , an ' she turn round on I an ' say : ' tha ' young vixen , tha ' ! there tha ' stand sayin ' tha ' do not   like this one an ' tha ' do not   like that one . how do tha ' like thysel ' ? ' it make I laugh an ' it bring I to my sens in a minute . " 

 she go away in high spirit as soon as she have give Mary her breakfast . she be go to walk five mile across the moor to the cottage , and she be go to help her mother with the washing and do the week 's baking and enjoy herself thoroughly . 

 Mary feel lonely than ever when she know she be no long in the house . she go out into the garden as quickly as possible , and the first thing she do be to run round and round the fountain flower garden ten time . she count the time carefully and when she have finish she feel in well spirit . the sunshine make the whole place look different . the high , deep , blue sky arch over Misselthwaite as well as over the moor , and she keep lift her face and look up into it , try to imagine what it would be like to lie down on one of the little snow - white cloud and float about . she go into the first kitchen - garden and find Ben Weatherstaff work there with two other gardener . the change in the weather seem to have do he good . he speak to she of his own accord . " Springtime 's comin , ' " he say . " can not tha ' smell it ? " 

 Mary sniff and think she could . 

 " I smell something nice and fresh and damp , " she say . 

 " that be th ' good rich earth , " he answer , dig away . " it be in a good humor makin ' ready to grow thing . it be glad when plantin ' time come . it be dull in th ' winter when it be get nowt to do . in th ' flower garden out there thing will be stirrin ' down below in th ' dark . Th ' sun 's warmin ' them . you will see bit o ' green spike stickin ' out o ' th ' black earth after a bit . " 

 " what will they be ? " ask Mary . 

 " crocuse an ' snowdrop an ' daffydowndilly . have tha ' never see they ? " 

 " no . everything be hot , and wet , and green after the rain in India , " say Mary . " and I think thing grow up in a night . " 

 " these will not   grow up in a night , " say Weatherstaff . " Tha'll have to wait for them . they will poke up a bit high here , an ' push out a spike more there , an ' uncurl a leaf this day an ' another that . you watch them . " 

 " I be go to , " answer Mary . 

 very soon she hear the soft rustle flight of wing again and she know at once that the robin have come again . he be very pert and lively , and hop about so close to her foot , and put his head on one side and look at she so slyly that she ask Ben Weatherstaff a question . 

 " do you think he remember I ? " she say . 

 " Remembers thee ! " say Weatherstaff indignantly . " he know every cabbage stump in th ' garden , let alone th ' people . he be never see a little wench here before , an ' he be bent on findin ' out all about thee . Tha 's no need to try to hide anything from he . " 

 " be thing stir down below in the dark in that garden where he live ? " Mary inquire . 

 " what garden ? " grunt Weatherstaff , become surly again . 

 " the one where the old rose - tree be . " she could not help ask , because she want so much to know . " be all the flower dead , or do some of they come again in the summer ? be there ever any rose ? " 

 " ask he , " say Ben Weatherstaff , hunch his shoulder toward the robin . " he be the only one as know . no one else have see inside it for ten year ' . " 

 ten year be a long time , Mary think . she have be bear ten year ago . 

 she walk away , slowly think . she have begin to like the garden just as she have begin to like the robin and Dickon and Martha 's mother . she be begin to like Martha , too . that seem a good many people to like when you be not use to like . she think of the robin as one of the people . she go to her walk outside the long , ivy - cover wall over which she could see the tree - top ; and the second time she walk up and down the most interesting and exciting thing happen to she , and it be all through Ben Weatherstaff 's robin . 

 she hear a chirp and a twitter , and when she look at the bare flower - bed at her left side there he be hop about and pretend to peck thing out of the earth to persuade she that he have not follow she . but she know he have follow she and the surprise so fill she with delight that she almost tremble a little . 

 " you do remember I ! " she cry out . " you do ! you be pretty than anything else in the world ! " 

 she chirp , and talk , and coax and he hop , and flirt his tail and twitter . it be as if he be talk . his red waistcoat be like satin and he puff his tiny breast out and be so fine and so grand and so pretty that it be really as if he be show she how important and like a human person a robin could be . Mistress Mary forget that she have ever be contrary in her life when he allow she to draw close and close to he , and bend down and talk and try to make something like robin sound . 

 oh ! to think that he should actually let she come as near to he as that ! he know nothing in the world would make she put out her hand toward he or startle he in the least tiny way . he know it because he be a real person only nice than any other person in the world . she be so happy that she scarcely dare to breathe . 

 the flower - bed be not quite bare . it be bare of flower because the perennial plant have be cut down for their winter rest , but there be tall shrub and low one which grow together at the back of the bed , and as the robin hop about under they she see he hop over a small pile of freshly turn up earth . he stop on it to look for a worm . the earth have be turn up because a dog have be try to dig up a mole and he have scratch quite a deep hole . 

 Mary look at it , not really know why the hole be there , and as she look she see something almost bury in the newly - turn soil . it be something like a ring of rusty iron or brass and when the robin fly up into a tree nearby she put out her hand and pick the ring up . it be more than a ring , however ; it be an old key which look as if it have be bury a long time . 

 Mistress Mary stand up and look at it with an almost frightened face as it hang from her finger . 

 " perhaps it have be bury for ten year , " she say in a whisper . " perhaps it be the key to the garden ! " 




 CHAPTER VIII 

 the ROBIN who show the WAY 

 she look at the key quite a long time . she turn it over and over , and think about it . as I have say before , she be not a child who have be train to ask permission or consult her elder about thing . all she think about the key be that if it be the key to the closed garden , and she could find out where the door be , she could perhaps open it and see what be inside the wall , and what have happen to the old rose - tree . it be because it have be shut up so long that she want to see it . it seem as if it must be different from other place and that something strange must have happen to it during ten year . besides that , if she like it she could go into it every day and shut the door behind she , and she could make up some play of her own and play it quite alone , because nobody would ever know where she be , but would think the door be still lock and the key bury in the earth . the thought of that please she very much . 

 live as it be , all by herself in a house with a hundred mysteriously close room and have nothing whatever to do to amuse herself , have set her inactive brain to work and be actually awaken her imagination . there be no doubt that the fresh , strong , pure air from the moor have a great deal to do with it . just as it have give she an appetite , and fight with the wind have stir her blood , so the same thing have stir her mind . in India she have always be too hot and languid and weak to care much about anything , but in this place she be begin to care and to want to do new thing . already she feel less " contrary , " though she do not know why . 

 she put the key in her pocket and walk up and down her walk . no one but herself ever seem to come there , so she could walk slowly and look at the wall , or , rather , at the ivy grow on it . the ivy be the baffle thing . Howsoever carefully she look she could see nothing but thickly grow , glossy , dark green leaf . she be very much disappointed . something of her contrariness come back to she as she pace the walk and look over it at the tree - top inside . it seem so silly , she say to herself , to be near it and not be able to get in . she take the key in her pocket when she go back to the house , and she make up her mind that she would always carry it with she when she go out , so that if she ever should find the hidden door she would be ready . 

 Mrs. Medlock have allow Martha to sleep all night at the cottage , but she be back at her work in the morning with cheek red than ever and in the good of spirit . 

 " I get up at four o'clock , " she say . " eh ! it be pretty on th ' moor with th ' bird gettin ' up an ' th ' rabbit scamperin ' about an ' th ' sun risin ' . I do not   walk all th ' way . a man give I a ride in his cart an ' I do enjoy myself . " 

 she be full of story of the delight of her day out . her mother have be glad to see she and they have get the baking and wash all out of the way . she have even make each of the child a doughcake with a bit of brown sugar in it . 

 " I have them all pipin ' hot when they come in from playin ' on th ' moor . an ' th ' cottage all smell o ' nice , clean hot bakin ' an ' there be a good fire , an ' they just shout for joy . our Dickon he say our cottage be good enough for a king . " 

 in the evening they have all sit round the fire , and Martha and her mother have sew patch on tear clothe and mend stocking and Martha have tell they about the little girl who have come from India and who have be wait on all her life by what Martha call " black " until she do not   know how to put on her own stocking . 

 " eh ! they do like to hear about you , " say Martha . " they want to know all about th ' black an ' about th ' ship you come in . I could not   tell them enough . " 

 Mary reflect a little . 

 " I will tell you a great deal more before your next day out , " she say , ' so that you will have more to talk about . I dare say they would like to hear about rid on elephant and camel , and about the officer go to hunt tiger . " 

 " my word ! " cry delight Martha . " it would set them clean off their head . would tha ' really do that , Miss ? it would be same as a wild beast show like we hear they have in York once . " 

 " India be quite different from Yorkshire , " Mary say slowly , as she think the matter over . " I never think of that . do Dickon and your mother like to hear you talk about I ? " 

 " why , our Dickon 's eye nearly start out o ' his head , they get that round , " answer Martha . " but mother , she be put out about your seemin ' to be all by yourself like . she say , ' have not   Mr. Craven get no governess for she , nor no nurse ? ' and I say , ' no , he have not , though Mrs. Medlock say he will when he think of it , but she say he may not   think of it for two or three year . ' " 

 " I do not   want a governess , " say Mary sharply . 

 " but mother say you ought to be learnin ' your book by this time an ' you ought to have a woman to look after you , an ' she say : ' now , Martha , you just think how you would feel yourself , in a big place like that , wanderin ' about all alone , an ' no mother . you do your good to cheer she up , ' she say , an ' I say I would . " 

 Mary give she a long , steady look . 

 " you do cheer I up , " she say . " I like to hear you talk . " 

 presently Martha go out of the room and come back with something hold in her hand under her apron . 

 " what do tha ' think , " she say , with a cheerful grin . " I have   bring thee a present . " 

 " a present ! " exclaim Mistress Mary . how could a cottage full of fourteen hungry people give any one a present ! 

 " a man be drivin ' across the moor peddlin ' , " Martha explain . " an ' he stop his cart at our door . he have pot an ' pan an ' odd an ' end , but mother have no money to buy anythin ' . just as he be go away our ' Lizabeth Ellen call out , ' Mother , he be get skippin'-ropes with red an ' blue handle . ' an ' mother she call out quite sudden , ' here , stop , mister ! how much be they ? ' an ' he say ' Tuppence ' , an ' mother she begin fumblin ' in her pocket an ' she say to I , ' Martha , tha 's bring I thy wage like a good lass , an ' I have   get four place to put every penny , but I be just go to take tuppence out of it to buy that child a skippin'-rope , ' an ' she buy one an ' here it be . " 

 she bring it out from under her apron and exhibit it quite proudly . it be a strong , slender rope with a strip red and blue handle at each end , but Mary Lennox have never see a skipping - rope before . she gaze at it with a mystified expression . 

 " what be it for ? " she ask curiously . 

 " for ! " cry out Martha . " do tha ' mean that they have   not get skippin'-ropes in India , for all they have   get elephant and tiger and camel ! no wonder most of them 's black . this be what it be for ; just watch I . " 

 and she run into the middle of the room and , take a handle in each hand , begin to skip , and skip , and skip , while Mary turn in her chair to stare at she , and the queer face in the old portrait seem to stare at she , too , and wonder what on earth this common little cottager have the impudence to be do under their very nose . but Martha do not even see they . the interest and curiosity in Mistress Mary 's face delight she , and she go on skip and count as she skip until she have reach a hundred . 

 " I could skip long than that , " she say when she stop . " I have   skip as much as five hundred when I be twelve , but I be not   as fat then as I be now , an ' I be in practice . " 

 Mary get up from her chair begin to feel excited herself . 

 " it look nice , " she say . " your mother be a kind woman . do you think I could ever skip like that ? " 

 " you just try it , " urge Martha , hand she the skipping - rope . " you can not   skip a hundred at first , but if you practice you will mount up . that be what mother say . she say , ' nothing will do she more good than skippin ' rope . it be th ' sensible toy a child can have . let she play out in th ' fresh air skippin ' an ' it will stretch her leg an ' arm an ' give she some strength in them . ' " 

 it be plain that there be not a great deal of strength in Mistress Mary 's arm and leg when she first begin to skip . she be not very clever at it , but she like it so much that she do not want to stop . 

 " put on tha ' thing and run an ' skip out o ' door , " say Martha . " Mother say I must tell you to keep out o ' door as much as you could , even when it rain a bit , so as tha ' wrap up warm . " 

 Mary put on her coat and hat and take her skipping - rope over her arm . she open the door to go out , and then suddenly think of something and turn back rather slowly . 

 " Martha , " she say , " they be your wage . it be your two - pence really . thank you . " she say it stiffly because she be not use to thank people or notice that they do thing for she . " thank you , " she say , and hold out her hand because she do not know what else to do . 

 Martha give her hand a clumsy little shake , as if she be not accustomed to this sort of thing either . then she laugh . 

 " eh ! th ' art a queer , old - womanish thing , " she say . " if tha'd be our ' Lizabeth Ellen tha'd have give I a kiss . " 

 Mary look stiff than ever . 

 " do you want I to kiss you ? " 

 Martha laugh again . 

 " Nay , not I , " she answer . " if tha ' be different , p'raps tha'd want to thysel ' . but tha ' be not . run off outside an ' play with thy rope . " 

 Mistress Mary feel a little awkward as she go out of the room . yorkshire people seem strange , and Martha be always rather a puzzle to she . at first she have dislike she very much , but now she do not . the skipping - rope be a wonderful thing . she count and skip , and skip and count , until her cheek be quite red , and she be more interested than she have ever be since she be bear . the sun be shin and a little wind be blow not a rough wind , but one which come in delightful little gust and bring a fresh scent of newly turn earth with it . she skip round the fountain garden , and up one walk and down another . she skip at last into the kitchen - garden and see Ben Weatherstaff dig and talk to his robin , which be hop about he . she skip down the walk toward he and he lift his head and look at she with a curious expression . she have wonder if he would notice she . she want he to see her skip . 

 " well ! " he exclaim . " upon my word . p'rap tha ' art a young ' un , after all , an ' p'raps tha 's get child 's blood in thy vein instead of sour buttermilk . Tha 's skip red into thy cheek as sure as my name 's Ben Weatherstaff . I would not   have believe tha ' could do it . " 

 " I never skip before , " Mary say . " I be just begin . I can only go up to twenty . " 

 " Tha ' keep on , " say Ben . " Tha ' shape well enough at it for a young ' un that be live with heathen . just see how he be watchin ' thee , " jerk his head toward the robin . " he follow after thee yesterday . he will be at it again today . he will be bind to find out what th ' skippin'-rope be . he be never see one . eh ! " shake his head at the bird , " tha ' curiosity will be th ' death of thee sometime if tha ' do not   look sharp . " 

 Mary skip round all the garden and round the orchard , rest every few minute . at length she go to her own special walk and make up her mind to try if she could skip the whole length of it . it be a good long skip and she begin slowly , but before she have go half - way down the path she be so hot and breathless that she be oblige to stop . she do not mind much , because she have already count up to thirty . she stop with a little laugh of pleasure , and there , lo and behold , be the robin sway on a long branch of ivy . he have follow she and he greet she with a chirp . as Mary have skip toward he she feel something heavy in her pocket strike against she at each jump , and when she see the robin she laugh again . 

 " you show I where the key be yesterday , " she say . " you ought to show I the door today ; but I do not   believe you know ! " 

 the robin fly from his swing spray of ivy on to the top of the wall and he open his beak and sing a loud , lovely trill , merely to show off . nothing in the world be quite as adorably lovely as a robin when he show off and they be nearly always do it . 

 Mary Lennox have hear a great deal about Magic in her ayah 's story , and she always say that what happen almost at that moment be magic . 

 one of the nice little gust of wind rush down the walk , and it be a strong one than the rest . it be strong enough to wave the branch of the tree , and it be more than strong enough to sway the trail spray of untrimmed ivy hang from the wall . Mary have step close to the robin , and suddenly the gust of wind swing aside some loose ivy trail , and more suddenly still she jump toward it and catch it in her hand . this she do because she have see something under it a round knob which have be cover by the leaf hang over it . it be the knob of a door . 

 she put her hand under the leaf and begin to pull and push they aside . thick as the ivy hung , it nearly all be a loose and swing curtain , though some have creep over wood and iron . Mary 's heart begin to thump and her hand to shake a little in her delight and excitement . the robin keep sing and twitter away and tilt his head on one side , as if he be as excited as she be . what be this under her hand which be square and make of iron and which her finger find a hole in ? 

 it be the lock of the door which have be close ten year and she put her hand in her pocket , draw out the key and find it fit the keyhole . she put the key in and turn it . it take two hand to do it , but it do turn . 

 and then she take a long breath and look behind she up the long walk to see if any one be come . no one be come . no one ever do come , it seem , and she take another long breath , because she could not help it , and she hold back the swing curtain of ivy and push back the door which open slowly slowly . 

 then she slip through it , and shut it behind she , and stand with she back against it , look about she and breathe quite fast with excitement , and wonder , and delight . 

 she be stand inside the secret garden . 




 CHAPTER IX 

 the STRANGEST HOUSE any one ever live in 

 it be the sweetest , most mysterious - look place any one could imagine . the high wall which shut it in be cover with the leafless stem of climb rose which be so thick that they be mat together . Mary Lennox know they be rose because she have see a great many rose in India . all the ground be cover with grass of a wintry brown and out of it grow clump of bush which be surely rosebush if they be alive . there be number of standard rose which have so spread their branch that they be like little tree . there be other tree in the garden , and one of the thing which make the place look strangest and loveliest be that climb rose have run all over they and swing down long tendril which make light swaying curtain , and here and there they have catch at each other or at a far - reach branch and have creep from one tree to another and make lovely bridge of themselves . there be neither leaf nor rose on they now and Mary do not know whether they be dead or alive , but their thin gray or brown branch and spray look like a sort of hazy mantle spread over everything , wall , and tree , and even brown grass , where they have fall from their fastening and run along the ground . it be this hazy tangle from tree to tree which make it all look so mysterious . Mary have think it must be different from other garden which have not be leave all by themselves so long ; and indeed it be different from any other place she have ever see in her life . 

 " how still it be ! " she whisper . " how still ! " 

 then she wait a moment and listen at the stillness . the robin , who have fly to his treetop , be still as all the rest . he do not even flutter his wing ; he sit without stir , and look at Mary . 

 " no wonder it be still , " she whisper again . " I be the first person who have speak in here for ten year . " 

 she move away from the door , step as softly as if she be afraid of awaken some one . she be glad that there be grass under her foot and that her step make no sound . she walk under one of the fairy - like gray arch between the tree and look up at the spray and tendril which form they . " I wonder if they be all quite dead , " she say . " be it all a quite dead garden ? I wish it be not . " 

 if she have be Ben Weatherstaff she could have tell whether the wood be alive by look at it , but she could only see that there be only gray or brown spray and branch and none show any sign of even a tiny leaf - bud anywhere . 

 but she be inside the wonderful garden and she could come through the door under the ivy any time and she feel as if she have find a world all her own . 

 the sun be shin inside the four wall and the high arch of blue sky over this particular piece of Misselthwaite seem even more brilliant and soft than it be over the moor . the robin fly down from his tree - top and hop about or fly after she from one bush to another . he chirp a good deal and have a very busy air , as if he be show her thing . everything be strange and silent and she seem to be hundred of mile away from any one , but somehow she do not feel lonely at all . all that trouble she be her wish that she know whether all the rose be dead , or if perhaps some of they have live and might put out leaf and bud as the weather get warm . she do not want it to be a quite dead garden . if it be a quite alive garden , how wonderful it would be , and what thousand of rose would grow on every side ! 

 her skipping - rope have hang over her arm when she come in and after she have walk about for a while she think she would skip round the whole garden , stop when she want to look at thing . there seem to have be grass path here and there , and in one or two corner there be alcove of evergreen with stone seat or tall moss - cover flower urn in they . 

 as she come near the second of these alcove she stop skip . there have once be a flowerbed in it , and she think she see something stick out of the black earth some sharp little pale green point . she remember what Ben Weatherstaff have say and she kneel down to look at they . 

 " yes , they be tiny grow thing and they might be crocus or snowdrop or daffodil , " she whisper . 

 she bent very close to they and sniff the fresh scent of the damp earth . she like it very much . 

 " perhaps there be some other one come up in other place , " she say . " I will go all over the garden and look . " 

 she do not skip , but walk . she go slowly and keep her eye on the ground . she look in the old border bed and among the grass , and after she have go round , try to miss nothing , she have find ever so many more sharp , pale green point , and she have become quite excited again . 

 " it be not   a quite dead garden , " she cry out softly to herself . " even if the rose be dead , there be other thing alive . " 

 she do not know anything about gardening , but the grass seem so thick in some of the place where the green point be push their way through that she think they do not seem to have room enough to grow . she search about until she find a rather sharp piece of wood and kneel down and dig and weed out the weed and grass until she make nice little clear place around they . 

 " now they look as if they could breathe , " she say , after she have finish with the first one . " I be go to do ever so many more . I will do all I can see . if I have not   time today I can come tomorrow . " 

 she go from place to place , and dig and weed , and enjoy herself so immensely that she be lead on from bed to bed and into the grass under the tree . the exercise make she so warm that she first throw her coat off , and then her hat , and without know it she be smile down on to the grass and the pale green point all the time . 

 the robin be tremendously busy . he be very much pleased to see gardening begin on his own estate . he have often wonder at Ben Weatherstaff . where gardening be do all sort of delightful thing to eat be turn up with the soil . now here be this new kind of creature who be not half Ben 's size and yet have have the sense to come into his garden and begin at once . 

 Mistress Mary work in her garden until it be time to go to her midday dinner . in fact , she be rather late in remembering , and when she put on her coat and hat , and pick up her skipping - rope , she could not believe that she have be work two or three hour . she have be actually happy all the time ; and dozen and dozen of the tiny , pale green point be to be see in clear place , look twice as cheerful as they have look before when the grass and weed have be smother they . 

 " I shall come back this afternoon , " she say , look all round at her new kingdom , and speak to the tree and the rose - bush as if they hear she . 

 then she run lightly across the grass , push open the slow old door and slip through it under the ivy . she have such red cheek and such bright eye and eat such a dinner that Martha be delighted . 

 " two piece o ' meat an ' two help o ' rice puddin ' ! " she say . " Eh ! mother will be pleased when I tell she what th ' skippin'-rope 's do for thee . " 

 in the course of she dig with her pointed stick Mistress Mary have find herself dig up a sort of white root rather like an onion . she have put it back in its place and pat the earth carefully down on it and just now she wonder if Martha could tell she what it be . 

 " Martha , " she say , " what be those white root that look like onion ? " 

 " they be bulb , " answer Martha . " lot o ' spring flower grow from them . th ' very little one be snowdrop an ' crocus an ' th ' big one be narcissus an ' jonquils and daffydowndilly . Th ' big of all be lily an ' purple flag . eh ! they be nice . Dickon 's get a whole lot of them plant in our bit o ' garden . " 

 " do Dickon know all about they ? " ask Mary , a new idea take possession of she . 

 " our Dickon can make a flower grow out of a brick walk . Mother say he just whisper thing out o ' th ' ground . " 

 " do bulb live a long time ? would they live year and year if no one help they ? " inquire Mary anxiously . 

 " they be thing as help themselves , " say Martha . " that be why poor folk can afford to have them . if you do not   trouble them , most of ' em'll work away underground for a lifetime an ' spread out an ' have little ' un . there be a place in th ' park wood here where there be snowdrop by thousand . they be the prettiest sight in Yorkshire when th ' spring come . no one know when they be first plant . " 

 " I wish the spring be here now , " say Mary . " I want to see all the thing that grow in England . " 

 she have finish her dinner and go to her favorite seat on the hearth - rug . 

 " I wish I wish I have a little spade , " she say . " whatever do tha ' want a spade for ? " ask Martha , laugh . " art tha ' go to take to diggin ' ? I must tell mother that , too . " 

 Mary look at the fire and ponder a little . she must be careful if she mean to keep her secret kingdom . she be not   do any harm , but if Mr. Craven find out about the open door he would be fearfully angry and get a new key and lock it up forevermore . she really could not bear that . 

 " this be such a big lonely place , " she say slowly , as if she be turn matter over in her mind . " the house be lonely , and the park be lonely , and the garden be lonely . so many place seem shut up . I never do many thing in India , but there be more people to look at native and soldier march by and sometimes band playing , and my Ayah tell I story . there be no one to talk to here except you and Ben Weatherstaff . and you have to do your work and Ben Weatherstaff will not   speak to I often . I think if I have a little spade I could dig somewhere as he do , and I might make a little garden if he would give I some seed . " 

 Martha 's face quite light up . 

 " there now ! " she exclaim , " if that be not   one of th ' thing mother say . she say , ' there be such a lot o ' room in that big place , why do not   they give she a bit for herself , even if she do not   plant nothing but parsley an ' radish ? she would dig an ' rake away an ' be right down happy over it . ' they be the very word she say . " 

 " be they ? " say Mary . " how many thing she know , do not   she ? " 

 " eh ! " say Martha . " it be like she say : ' a woman as bring up twelve child learn something besides her A B C. Children 's as good as ' rithmetic to set you findin ' out thing . ' " 

 " how much would a spade cost a little one ? " Mary ask . 

 " well , " be Martha 's reflective answer , " at Thwaite village there be a shop or so an ' I see little garden set with a spade an ' a rake an ' a fork all tie together for two shilling . an ' they be stout enough to work with , too . " 

 " I have   get more than that in my purse , " say Mary . " Mrs. Morrison give I five shilling and Mrs. Medlock give I some money from Mr. Craven . " 

 " do he remember thee that much ? " exclaim Martha . 

 " Mrs. Medlock say I be to have a shilling a week to spend . she give I one every Saturday . I do not   know what to spend it on . " 

 " my word ! that be rich , " say Martha . " Tha ' can buy anything in th ' world tha ' want . th ' rent of our cottage be only one an ' threepence an ' it be like pullin ' eye - tooth to get it . now I have   just think of something , " put her hand on her hip . 

 " what ? " say Mary eagerly . 

 " in the shop at Thwaite they sell package o ' flower - seed for a penny each , and our Dickon he know which be th ' prettiest one an ' how to make them grow . he walk over to Thwaite many a day just for th ' fun of it . do tha ' know how to print letter ? " suddenly . 

 " I know how to write , " Mary answer . 

 Martha shake her head . 

 " our Dickon can only read printin ' . if tha ' could print we could write a letter to he an ' ask he to go an ' buy th ' garden tool an ' th ' seed at th ' same time . " 

 " oh ! you be a good girl ! " Mary cry . " you be , really ! I do not   know you be so nice . I know I can print letter if I try . let us ask Mrs. Medlock for a pen and ink and some paper . " 

 " I have   get some of my own , " say Martha . " I buy them so I could print a bit of a letter to mother of a Sunday . I will go and get it . " she run out of the room , and Mary stand by the fire and twist her thin little hand together with sheer pleasure . 

 " if I have a spade , " she whisper , " I can make the earth nice and soft and dig up weed . if I have seed and can make flower grow the garden will not   be dead at all it will come alive . " 

 she do not go out again that afternoon because when Martha return with her pen and ink and paper she be oblige to clear the table and carry the plate and dish downstairs and when she get into the kitchen Mrs. Medlock be there and tell she to do something , so Mary wait for what seem to she a long time before she come back . then it be a serious piece of work to write to Dickon . Mary have be teach very little because her governess have dislike she too much to stay with she . she could not spell particularly well but she find that she could print letter when she try . this be the letter Martha dictate to she : " my Dear Dickon : 

 this come hop to find you well as it leave I at present . Miss Mary have plenty of money and will you go to Thwaite and buy she some flower seed and a set of garden tool to make a flower - bed . pick the prettiest one and easy to grow because she have never do it before and live in India which be different . give my love to mother and every one of you . Miss Mary be go to tell I a lot more so that on my next day out you can hear about elephant and camel and gentleman go hunt lion and tiger . 

 " your love sister , 
  Martha Phoebe Sowerby . " 
 " we will put the money in th ' envelope an ' I will get th ' butcher boy to take it in his cart . he be a great friend o ' Dickon 's , " say Martha . 

 " how shall I get the thing when Dickon buy they ? " 

 " he will bring them to you himself . he will like to walk over this way . " 

 " oh ! " exclaim Mary , " then I shall see he ! I never think I should see Dickon . " 

 " do tha ' want to see he ? " ask Martha suddenly , for Mary have look so pleased . 

 " yes , I do . I never see a boy fox and crow love . I want to see he very much . " 

 Martha give a little start , as if she remember something . " now to think , " she break out , " to think o ' I forgettin ' that there ; an ' I think I be go to tell you first thing this mornin ' . I ask mother and she say she would ask Mrs. Medlock her own self . " 

 " do you mean " Mary begin . 

 " what I say Tuesday . ask she if you might be drive over to our cottage some day and have a bit o ' mother 's hot oat cake , an ' butter , an ' a glass o ' milk . " 

 it seem as if all the interesting thing be happen in one day . to think of go over the moor in the daylight and when the sky be blue ! to think of go into the cottage which hold twelve child ! 

 " do she think Mrs. Medlock would let I go ? " she ask , quite anxiously . 

 " Aye , she think she would . she know what a tidy woman mother be and how clean she keep the cottage . " 

 " if I go I should see your mother as well as Dickon , " say Mary , think it over and like the idea very much . " she do not   seem to be like the mother in India . " 

 her work in the garden and the excitement of the afternoon end by make she feel quiet and thoughtful . Martha stay with she until tea - time , but they sit in comfortable quiet and talk very little . but just before Martha go downstairs for the tea - tray , Mary ask a question . 

 " Martha , " she say , " have the scullery - maid have the toothache again today ? " 

 Martha certainly start slightly . 

 " what make thee ask that ? " she say . 

 " because when I wait so long for you to come back I open the door and walk down the corridor to see if you be come . and I hear that far - off cry again , just as we hear it the other night . there be not   a wind today , so you see it could not   have be the wind . " 

 " eh ! " say Martha restlessly . " Tha ' must not   go walkin ' about in corridor an ' listenin ' . Mr. Craven would be that there angry there be no knowin ' what he would do . " 

 " I be not   listen , " say Mary . " I be just wait for you and I hear it . that be three time . " 

 " my word ! there be Mrs. Medlock 's bell , " say Martha , and she almost run out of the room . 

 " it be the strange house any one ever live in , " say Mary drowsily , as she drop her head on the cushioned seat of the armchair near she . fresh air , and dig , and skip - rope have make she feel so comfortably tired that she fall asleep . 




 CHAPTER x 

 DICKON 

 the sun shine down for nearly a week on the secret garden . the Secret Garden be what Mary call it when she be think of it . she like the name , and she like still more the feeling that when its beautiful old wall shut she in no one know where she be . it seem almost like be shut out of the world in some fairy place . the few book she have read and like have be fairy - story book , and she have read of secret garden in some of the story . sometimes people go to sleep in they for a hundred year , which she have think must be rather stupid . she have no intention of go to sleep , and , in fact , she be become wider awake every day which pass at Misselthwaite . she be begin to like to be out of door ; she no long hat the wind , but enjoy it . she could run fast , and long , and she could skip up to a hundred . the bulb in the secret garden must have be much astonish . such nice clear place be make round they that they have all the breathing space they want , and really , if Mistress Mary have know it , they begin to cheer up under the dark earth and work tremendously . the sun could get at they and warm they , and when the rain come down it could reach they at once , so they begin to feel very much alive . 

 Mary be an odd , determined little person , and now she have something interesting to be determine about , she be very much absorb , indeed . she work and dig and pull up weed steadily , only become more pleased with her work every hour instead of tire of it . it seem to she like a fascinating sort of play . she find many more of the sprout pale green point than she have ever hop to find . they seem to be start up everywhere and each day she be sure she find tiny new one , some so tiny that they barely peep above the earth . there be so many that she remember what Martha have say about the ' snowdrop by the thousand , " and about bulb spread and make new one . these have be leave to themselves for ten year and perhaps they have spread , like the snowdrop , into thousand . she wonder how long it would be before they show that they be flower . sometimes she stop dig to look at the garden and try to imagine what it would be like when it be cover with thousand of lovely thing in bloom . during that week of sunshine , she become more intimate with Ben Weatherstaff . she surprise he several time by seem to start up beside he as if she spring out of the earth . the truth be that she be afraid that he would pick up his tool and go away if he see she come , so she always walk toward he as silently as possible . but , in fact , he do not object to she as strongly as he have at first . perhaps he be secretly rather flatter by her evident desire for his elderly company . then , also , she be more civil than she have be . he do not know that when she first see he she speak to he as she would have speak to a native , and have not know that a cross , sturdy old Yorkshire man be not accustomed to salaam to his master , and be merely command by they to do thing . 

 " tha'rt like th ' robin , " he say to her one morning when he lift his head and see she stand by he . " I never know when I shall see thee or which side tha'll come from . " 

 " he be friend with I now , " say Mary . 

 " that be like he , " snap Ben Weatherstaff . " Makin ' up to th ' woman folk just for vanity an ' flightiness . there be nothing he would not   do for th ' sake o ' showin ' off an ' flirtin ' his tail - feather . he be as full o ' pride as an egg 's full o ' meat . " 

 he very seldom talk much and sometimes do not even answer Mary 's question except by a grunt , but this morning he say more than usual . he stand up and rest one hobnail boot on the top of his spade while he look she over . 

 " how long have tha ' be here ? " he jerk out . 

 " I think it be about a month , " she answer . 

 " Tha 's beginnin ' to do Misselthwaite credit , " he say . " Tha 's a bit fat than tha ' be an ' tha 's not quite so yeller . tha ' look like a young pluck crow when tha ' first come into this garden . think I to myself I never set eye on an uglier , sourer face young ' un . " 

 Mary be not vain and as she have never think much of her look she be not greatly disturb . 

 " I know I be fat , " she say . " my stocking be get tight . they use to make wrinkle . there be the robin , Ben Weatherstaff . " 

 there , indeed , be the robin , and she think he look nice than ever . his red waistcoat be as glossy as satin and he flirt his wing and tail and tilt his head and hop about with all sort of lively grace . he seem determined to make Ben Weatherstaff admire he . but Ben be sarcastic . 

 " Aye , there tha ' art ! " he say . " Tha ' can put up with I for a bit sometimes when tha 's get no one well . Tha 's be reddenin ' up thy waistcoat an ' polishin ' thy feather this two week . I know what tha 's up to . Tha 's courtin ' some bold young madam somewhere tellin ' thy lie to she about bein ' th ' fine cock robin on Missel Moor an ' ready to fight all th ' rest of them . " 

 " oh ! look at he ! " exclaim Mary . 

 the robin be evidently in a fascinating , bold mood . he hop close and close and look at Ben Weatherstaff more and more engagingly . he fly on to the near currant bush and tilt his head and sing a little song right at he . 

 " Tha ' think tha'll get over I by do that , " say Ben , wrinkle his face up in such a way that Mary feel sure he be try not to look pleased . " Tha ' think no one can stand out against thee that be what tha ' think . " 

 the robin spread his wing Mary could scarcely believe her eye . he fly right up to the handle of Ben Weatherstaff 's spade and alight on the top of it . then the old man 's face wrinkle itself slowly into a new expression . he stand still as if he be afraid to breathe as if he would not have stir for the world , lest his robin should start away . he speak quite in a whisper . 

 " well , I be dange ! " he say as softly as if he be say something quite different . " Tha ' do know how to get at a chap tha ' do ! Tha 's fair unearthly , tha 's so knowin ' . " 

 and he stand without stir almost without draw his breath until the robin give another flirt to his wing and fly away . then he stand look at the handle of the spade as if there might be Magic in it , and then he begin to dig again and say nothing for several minute . 

 but because he keep break into a slow grin now and then , Mary be not afraid to talk to he . 

 " have you a garden of your own ? " she ask . 

 " no . I be bachelder an ' lodge with Martin at th ' gate . " 

 " if you have one , " say Mary , " what would you plant ? " 

 " cabbage an ' ' tater an ' onion . " 

 " but if you want to make a flower garden , " persist Mary , " what would you plant ? " 

 " Bulbs an ' sweet - smellin ' thing but mostly rose . " 

 Mary 's face light up . 

 " do you like rose ? " she say . 

 Ben Weatherstaff root up a weed and throw it aside before he answer . 

 " well , yes , I do . I be learn that by a young lady I be gardener to . she have a lot in a place she be fond of , an ' she love them like they be child or robin . I have   see she bend over an ' kiss them . " he drag out another weed and scowl at it . " that be as much as ten year ' ago . " 

 " where be she now ? " ask Mary , much interested . 

 " Heaven , " he answer , and drive his spade deep into the soil , " ' cord to what parson say . " 

 " what happen to the rose ? " Mary ask again , more interested than ever . 

 " they be leave to themselves . " 

 Mary be become quite excited . 

 " do they quite die ? do rose quite die when they be leave to themselves ? " she venture . 

 " well , I would get to like them an ' I like she an ' she like them , " Ben Weatherstaff admit reluctantly . " once or twice a year I would go an ' work at them a bit prune them an ' dig about th ' root . they run wild , but they be in rich soil , so some of them live . " 

 " when they have no leaf and look gray and brown and dry , how can you tell whether they be dead or alive ? " inquire Mary . 

 " wait till th ' spring get at them wait till th ' sun shin on th ' rain and th ' rain fall on th ' sunshine an ' then tha'll find out . " 

 " how how ? " cry Mary , forget to be careful . " look along th ' twig an ' branch an ' if tha ' see a bit of a brown lump swell here an ' there , watch it after th ' warm rain an ' see what happen . " he stop suddenly and look curiously at her eager face . " why do tha ' care so much about rose an ' such , all of a sudden ? " he demand . 

 Mistress Mary feel her face grow red . she be almost afraid to answer . 

 " I I want to play that that I have a garden of my own , " she stammer . " I there be nothing for I to do . I have nothing and no one . " 

 " well , " say Ben Weatherstaff slowly , as he watch she , " that be true . Tha ' have not . " 

 he say it in such an odd way that Mary wonder if he be actually a little sorry for she . she have never feel sorry for herself ; she have only feel tired and cross , because she dislike people and thing so much . but now the world seem to be change and get nice . if no one find out about the secret garden , she should enjoy herself always . 

 she stay with he for ten or fifteen minute long and ask he as many question as she dare . he answer every one of they in his queer grunt way and he do not seem really cross and do not pick up his spade and leave she . he say something about rose just as she be go away and it remind she of the one he have say he have be fond of . 

 " do you go and see those other rose now ? " she ask . 

 " not be this year . my rheumatic have make I too stiff in th ' joint . " 

 he say it in his grumble voice , and then quite suddenly he seem to get angry with she , though she do not see why he should . 

 " now look here ! " he say sharply . " do not   tha ' ask so many question . tha'rt th ' bad wench for askin ' question I have   ever come a cross . get thee go an ' play thee . I have   do talkin ' for today . " 

 and he say it so crossly that she know there be not the least use in stay another minute . she go skip slowly down the outside walk , think he over and say to herself that , queer as it be , here be another person whom she like in spite of his crossness . she like old Ben Weatherstaff . yes , she do like he . she always want to try to make he talk to she . also she begin to believe that he know everything in the world about flower . 

 there be a laurel - hedge walk which curve round the secret garden and end at a gate which open into a wood , in the park . she think she would slip round this walk and look into the wood and see if there be any rabbit hop about . she enjoy the skipping very much and when she reach the little gate she open it and go through because she hear a low , peculiar whistle sound and want to find out what it be . 

 it be a very strange thing indeed . she quite catch her breath as she stop to look at it . a boy be sit under a tree , with his back against it , play on a rough wooden pipe . he be a funny look boy about twelve . he look very clean and his nose turn up and his cheek be as red as poppy and never have Mistress Mary see such round and such blue eye in any boy 's face . and on the trunk of the tree he lean against , a brown squirrel be cling and watch he , and from behind a bush nearby a cock pheasant be delicately stretch his neck to peep out , and quite near he be two rabbit sit up and sniff with tremulous nose and actually it appear as if they be all draw near to watch he and listen to the strange low little call his pipe seem to make . 

 when he see Mary he hold up his hand and speak to she in a voice almost as low as and rather like his piping . 

 " do not   tha ' move , " he say . " it would flight them . " Mary remain motionless . he stop play his pipe and begin to rise from the ground . he move so slowly that it scarcely seem as though he be move at all , but at last he stand on his foot and then the squirrel scamper back up into the branch of his tree , the pheasant withdraw his head and the rabbit drop on all four and begin to hop away , though not at all as if they be frightened . 

 " I be Dickon , " the boy say . " I know tha'rt Miss Mary . " 

 then Mary realize that somehow she have know at first that he be Dickon . who else could have be charming rabbit and pheasant as the native charm snake in India ? he have a wide , red , curve mouth and his smile spread all over his face . 

 " I get up slow , " he explain , " because if tha ' make a quick move it startle them . a body ' as to move gentle an ' speak low when wild thing be about . " 

 he do not speak to she as if they have never see each other before but as if he know she quite well . Mary know nothing about boy and she speak to he a little stiffly because she feel rather shy . 

 " do you get Martha 's letter ? " she ask . 

 he nod his curly , rust - color head . " that be why I come . " 

 he stoop to pick up something which have be lie on the ground beside he when he pip . 

 " I have   get th ' garden tool . there be a little spade an ' rake an ' a fork an ' hoe . eh ! they be good ' un . there be a trowel , too . an ' th ' woman in th ' shop throw in a packet o ' white poppy an ' one o ' blue larkspur when I buy th ' other seed . " 

 " will you show the seed to I ? " Mary say . 

 she wish she could talk as he do . his speech be so quick and easy . it sound as if he like she and be not the least afraid she would not like he , though he be only a common moor boy , in patch clothe and with a funny face and a rough , rusty - red head . as she come close to he she notice that there be a clean fresh scent of heather and grass and leave about he , almost as if he be make of they . she like it very much and when she look into his funny face with the red cheek and round blue eye she forget that she have feel shy . 

 " let we sit down on this log and look at they , " she say . 

 they sit down and he take a clumsy little brown paper package out of his coat pocket . he untie the string and inside there be ever so many neater and small package with a picture of a flower on each one . 

 " there be a lot o ' mignonette an ' poppy , " he say . " Mignonette 's th ' sweetest smellin ' thing as grow , an ' it will grow wherever you cast it , same as poppy will . they as'll come up an ' bloom if you just whistle to them , they be th ' nicest of all . " he stop and turn his head quickly , his poppy - cheeked face light up . 

 " where be that robin as be callin ' us ? " he say . 

 the chirp come from a thick holly bush , bright with scarlet berry , and Mary think she know whose it be . 

 " be it really call we ? " she ask . 

 " Aye , " say Dickon , as if it be the most natural thing in the world , " he be callin ' some one he be friend with . that be same as sayin ' ' here I be . look at I . I want a bit of a chat . ' there he be in the bush . whose be he ? " 

 " he be Ben Weatherstaff 's , but I think he know I a little , " answer Mary . 

 " Aye , he know thee , " say Dickon in his low voice again . " an ' he like thee . he be take thee on . he will tell I all about thee in a minute . " 

 he move quite close to the bush with the slow movement Mary have notice before , and then he make a sound almost like the robin 's own twitter . the robin listen a few second , intently , and then answer quite as if he be reply to a question . 

 " Aye , he be a friend o ' your , " chuckle Dickon . 

 " do you think he be ? " cry Mary eagerly . she do so want to know . " do you think he really like I ? " 

 " he would not   come near thee if he do not , " answer Dickon . " bird be rare chooser an ' a robin can flout a body bad than a man . see , he be make up to thee now . ' can not tha ' see a chap ? ' he be sayin ' . " 

 and it really seem as if it must be true . he so sidle and twitter and tilt as he hop on his bush . 

 " do you understand everything bird say ? " say Mary . 

 Dickon 's grin spread until he seem all wide , red , curve mouth , and he rub his rough head . 

 " I think I do , and they think I do , " he say . " I have   live on th ' moor with them so long . I have   watch them break shell an ' come out an ' fledge an ' learn to fly an ' begin to sing , till I think I be one of them . sometimes I think p'raps I be a bird , or a fox , or a rabbit , or a squirrel , or even a beetle , an ' I do not   know it . " 

 he laugh and come back to the log and begin to talk about the flower seed again . he tell she what they look like when they be flower ; he tell she how to plant they , and watch they , and feed and water they . 

 " see here , " he say suddenly , turn round to look at she . " I will plant they for thee myself . where be tha ' garden ? " 

 Mary 's thin hand clutch each other as they lie on her lap . she do not know what to say , so for a whole minute she say nothing . she have never think of this . she feel miserable . and she feel as if she go red and then pale . 

 " Tha 's get a bit o ' garden , have not   tha ' ? " Dickon say . 

 it be true that she have turn red and then pale . Dickon see she do it , and as she still say nothing , he begin to be puzzle . 

 " would not   they give thee a bit ? " he ask . " have not   tha ' get any yet ? " 

 she hold her hand tighter and turn her eye toward he . 

 " I do not   know anything about boy , " she say slowly . " could you keep a secret , if I tell you one ? it be a great secret . I do not   know what I should do if any one find it out . I believe I should die ! " she say the last sentence quite fiercely . 

 Dickon look more puzzled than ever and even rub his hand over his rough head again , but he answer quite good - humoredly . " I be keepin ' secret all th ' time , " he say . " if I could not   keep secret from th ' other lad , secret about fox ' cub , an ' bird ' nest , an ' wild thing ' hole , there would be naught safe on th ' moor . Aye , I can keep secret . " 

 Mistress Mary do not mean to put out her hand and clutch his sleeve but she do it . 

 " I have   steal a garden , " she say very fast . " it be not   mine . it be not   anybody 's . nobody want it , nobody care for it , nobody ever go into it . perhaps everything be dead in it already . I do not   know . " 

 she begin to feel hot and as contrary as she have ever feel in her life . 

 " I do not   care , I do not   care ! nobody have any right to take it from I when I care about it and they do not . they be let it die , all shut in by itself , " she end passionately , and she throw her arm over her face and burst out cry - poor little Mistress Mary . 

 Dickon 's curious blue eye grow rounder and rounder . " eh - h - h ! " he say , draw his exclamation out slowly , and the way he do it mean both wonder and sympathy . 

 " I have   nothing to do , " say Mary . " nothing belong to I . I find it myself and I get into it myself . I be only just like the robin , and they would not   take it from the robin . " " where be it ? " ask Dickon in a drop voice . 

 Mistress Mary get up from the log at once . she know she feel contrary again , and obstinate , and she do not care at all . she be imperious and indian , and at the same time hot and sorrowful . 

 " come with I and I will show you , " she say . 

 she lead he round the laurel path and to the walk where the ivy grow so thickly . Dickon follow she with a queer , almost pity , look on his face . he feel as if he be be lead to look at some strange bird 's nest and must move softly . when she step to the wall and lift the hang ivy he start . there be a door and Mary push it slowly open and they pass in together , and then Mary stand and wave her hand round defiantly . 

 " it be this , " she say . " it be a secret garden , and I be the only one in the world who want it to be alive . " 

 Dickon look round and round about it , and round and round again . 

 " eh ! " he almost whisper , " it be a queer , pretty place ! it be like as if a body be in a dream . " 




 CHAPTER XI 

 the nest of the MISSEL thrush 

 for two or three minute he stand look round he , while Mary watch he , and then he begin to walk about softly , even more lightly than Mary have walk the first time she have find herself inside the four wall . his eye seem to be take in everything the gray tree with the gray creeper climb over they and hang from their branch , the tangle on the wall and among the grass , the evergreen alcove with the stone seat and tall flower urn stand in they . 

 " I never think I would see this place , " he say at last , in a whisper . 

 " do you know about it ? " ask Mary . 

 she have speak aloud and he make a sign to she . 

 " we must talk low , " he say , " or some one'll hear we an ' wonder what be to do in here . " 

 " oh ! I forget ! " say Mary , feel frightened and put her hand quickly against her mouth . " do you know about the garden ? " she ask again when she have recover herself . Dickon nod . 

 " Martha tell I there be one as no one ever go inside , " he answer . " Us use to wonder what it be like . " 

 he stop and look round at the lovely gray tangle about he , and his round eye look queerly happy . 

 " eh ! the nest as'll be here come springtime , " he say . " it would be th ' safe nestin ' place in England . no one never comin ' near an ' tangle o ' tree an ' rose to build in . I wonder all th ' bird on th ' moor do not   build here . " 

 Mistress Mary put her hand on his arm again without know it . 

 " will there be rose ? " she whisper . " can you tell ? I think perhaps they be all dead . " 

 " eh ! no ! not they not all of them ! " he answer . " look here ! " 

 he step over to the near tree an old , old one with gray lichen all over its bark , but uphold a curtain of tangle spray and branch . he take a thick knife out of his pocket and open one of its blade . 

 " there be lot o ' dead wood as ought to be cut out , " he say . " an ' there be a lot o ' old wood , but it make some new last year . this here be a new bit , " and he touch a shoot which look brownish green instead of hard , dry gray . Mary touch it herself in an eager , reverent way . 

 " that one ? " she say . " be that one quite alive quite ? " 

 Dickon curve his wide smile mouth . 

 " it be as wick as you or I , " he say ; and Mary remember that Martha have tell she that " wick " mean " alive " or " lively . " 

 " I be glad it be wick ! " she cry out in her whisper . " I want they all to be wick . let we go round the garden and count how many wick one there be . " 

 she quite pant with eagerness , and Dickon be as eager as she be . they go from tree to tree and from bush to bush . Dickon carry his knife in his hand and show her thing which she think wonderful . 

 " they have   run wild , " he say , " but th ' strong one have fair thrive on it . the delicatest one have die out , but th ' other have grow an ' grow , an ' spread an ' spread , till they be a wonder . see here ! " and he pull down a thick gray , dry - look branch . " a body might think this be dead wood , but I do not   believe it be down to th ' root . I will cut it low down an ' see . " 

 he kneel and with his knife cut the lifeless - look branch through , not far above the earth . 

 " there ! " he say exultantly . " I tell thee so . there be green in that wood yet . look at it . " 

 Mary be down on her knee before he speak , gaze with all her might . 

 " when it look a bit greenish an ' juicy like that , it be wick , " he explain . " when th ' inside be dry an ' break easy , like this here piece I have   cut off , it be do for . there be a big root here as all this live wood spring out of , an ' if th ' old wood 's cut off an ' it be dig round , and take care of there will be " he stop and lift his face to look up at the climbing and hang spray above he " there will be a fountain o ' rose here this summer . " 

 they go from bush to bush and from tree to tree . he be very strong and clever with his knife and know how to cut the dry and dead wood away , and could tell when an unpromising bough or twig have still green life in it . in the course of half an hour Mary think she could tell too , and when he cut through a lifeless - look branch she would cry out joyfully under her breath when she catch sight of the least shade of moist green . the spade , and hoe , and fork be very useful . he show she how to use the fork while he dig about root with the spade and stir the earth and let the air in . 

 they be work industriously round one of the big standard rose when he catch sight of something which make he utter an exclamation of surprise . 

 " why ! " he cry , point to the grass a few foot away . " who do that there ? " 

 it be one of Mary 's own little clearing round the pale green point . 

 " I do it , " say Mary . 

 " why , I think tha ' do not   know nothing about gardenin ' , " he exclaim . 

 " I do not , " she answer , " but they be so little , and the grass be so thick and strong , and they look as if they have no room to breathe . so I make a place for they . I do not   even know what they be . " 

 Dickon go and kneel down by they , smile his wide smile . 

 " Tha ' be right , " he say . " a gardener could not   have tell thee well . they will grow now like Jack 's bean - stalk . they be crocuse an ' snowdrop , an ' these here be narcissus , " turn to another patch , " an here 's daffydowndilly . eh ! they will be a sight . " 

 he run from one clearing to another . 

 " Tha ' have do a lot o ' work for such a little wench , " he say , look she over . 

 " I be grow fat , " say Mary , " and I be grow strong . I use always to be tired . when I dig I be not tired at all . I like to smell the earth when it be turn up . " 

 " it be rare good for thee , " he say , nod his head wisely . " there be naught as nice as th ' smell o ' good clean earth , except th ' smell o ' fresh growin ' thing when th ' rain fall on them . I get out on th ' moor many a day when it be rainin ' an ' I lie under a bush an ' listen to th ' soft swish o ' drop on th ' heather an ' I just sniff an ' sniff . my nose end fair quiver like a rabbit 's , mother say . " 

 " do you never catch cold ? " inquire Mary , gaze at he wonderingly . she have never see such a funny boy , or such a nice one . 

 " not I , " he say , grin . " I never ketche cold since I be bear . I be not   bring up nesh enough . I have   chase about th ' moor in all weather same as th ' rabbit do . Mother say I have   sniff up too much fresh air for twelve year ' to ever get to sniffin ' with cold . I be as tough as a white - thorn knobstick . " 

 he be work all the time he be talk and Mary be follow he and help he with her fork or the trowel . 

 " there be a lot of work to do here ! " he say once , look about quite exultantly . 

 " will you come again and help I to do it ? " Mary beg . " I be sure I can help , too . I can dig and pull up weed , and do whatever you tell I . oh ! do come , Dickon ! " 

 " I will come every day if tha ' want I , rain or shine , " he answer stoutly . " it be the good fun I ever have in my life shut in here an ' wakenin ' up a garden . " 

 " if you will come , " say Mary , " if you will help I to make it alive I will I do not   know what I will do , " she end helplessly . what could you do for a boy like that ? 

 " I will tell thee what tha'll do , " say Dickon , with his happy grin . " Tha'll get fat an ' tha'll get as hungry as a young fox an ' tha'll learn how to talk to th ' robin same as I do . eh ! we will have a lot o ' fun . " 

 he begin to walk about , look up in the tree and at the wall and bush with a thoughtful expression . 

 " I would not   want to make it look like a gardener 's garden , all clip an ' spick an ' span , would you ? " he say . " it be nice like this with thing runnin ' wild , an ' swingin ' an ' catchin ' hold of each other . " 

 " do not   let we make it tidy , " say Mary anxiously . " it would not   seem like a secret garden if it be tidy . " 

 Dickon stand rub his rusty - red head with a rather puzzled look . " it be a secret garden sure enough , " he say , " but seem like some one besides th ' robin must have be in it since it be shut up ten year ' ago . " 

 " but the door be lock and the key be bury , " say Mary . " no one could get in . " 

 " that be true , " he answer . " it be a queer place . seem to I as if there have be a bit o ' prunin ' do here an ' there , later than ten year ' ago . " 

 " but how could it have be do ? " say Mary . 

 he be examine a branch of a standard rise and he shake his head . 

 " Aye ! how could it ! " he murmur . " with th ' door lock an ' th ' key bury . " 

 Mistress Mary always feel that however many year she live she should never forget that first morning when her garden begin to grow . of course , it do seem to begin to grow for she that morning . when Dickon begin to clear place to plant seed , she remember what Basil have sing at she when he want to tease she . 

 " be there any flower that look like bell ? " she inquire . 

 " lily o ' th ' valley do , " he answer , dig away with the trowel , " an ' there be Canterbury bell , an ' campanulas . " 

 " let us plant some , " say Mary . " there 's lily o ' th , valley here already ; I see them . they will have grow too close an ' we will have to separate them , but there be plenty . Th ' other one take two year to bloom from seed , but I can bring you some bit o ' plant from our cottage garden . why do tha ' want them ? " 

 then Mary tell he about Basil and his brother and sister in India and of how she have hat they and of their call she " Mistress Mary Quite Contrary . " 

 " they use to dance round and sing at I . they sing 

 ' Mistress Mary , quite contrary , 
 how do your garden grow ? 
 with silver bell , and cockle shell , 
 and marigold all in a row . ' 
 I just remember it and it make I wonder if there be really flower like silver bell . " 

 she frown a little and give her trowel a rather spiteful dig into the earth . 

 " I be not   as contrary as they be . " 

 but Dickon laugh . 

 " eh ! " he say , and as he crumble the rich black soil she see he be sniff up the scent of it . " there do not   seem to be no need for no one to be contrary when there be flower an ' such like , an ' such lot o ' friendly wild thing runnin ' about makin ' home for themselves , or buildin ' nest an ' singin ' an ' whistlin ' , do there ? " 

 Mary , kneeling by he hold the seed , look at he and stop frown . 

 " Dickon , " she say , " you be as nice as Martha say you be . I like you , and you make the fifth person . I never think I should like five people . " 

 Dickon sit up on his heel as Martha do when she be polish the grate . he do look funny and delightful , Mary think , with his round blue eye and red cheek and happy look turn - up nose .

 CHAPTER XIII 

 " I be COLIN "
