 he have become quite excited and his strange eye begin to shine like star and look more immense than ever . 

 " they have to please I , " he say . " I will make they take I there and I will let you go , too . " 

 Mary 's hand clutch each other . everything would be spoil everything ! Dickon would never come back . she would never again feel like a missel thrush with a safe - hidden nest . 

 " oh , do not   do not   do not   do not   do that ! " she cry out . 

 he star as if he think she have go crazy ! 

 " why ? " he exclaim . " you say you want to see it . " 

 " I do , " she answer almost with a sob in her throat , " but if you make they open the door and take you in like that it will never be a secret again . " 

 he lean still far forward . 

 " a secret , " he say . " what do you mean ? tell I . " 

 Mary 's word almost tumble over one another . 

 " you see you see , " she pant , " if no one know but ourselves if there be a door , hide somewhere under the ivy if there be and we could find it ; and if we could slip through it together and shut it behind we , and no one know any one be inside and we call it our garden and pretend that that we be missel thrush and it be our nest , and if we play there almost every day and dig and plant seed and make it all come alive " 

 " be it dead ? " he interrupt she . 

 " it soon will be if no one care for it , " she go on . " the bulb will live but the rose " 

 he stop she again as excited as she be herself . 

 " what be bulb ? " he put in quickly . 

 " they be daffodil and lily and snowdrop . they be work in the earth now push up pale green point because the spring be come . " 

 " be the spring come ? " he say . " what be it like ? you do not   see it in room if you be ill . " 

 " it be the sun shin on the rain and the rain fall on the sunshine , and thing push up and work under the earth , " say Mary . " if the garden be a secret and we could get into it we could watch the thing grow big every day , and see how many rose be alive . do not   you see ? oh , do not   you see how much nice it would be if it be a secret ? " 

 he drop back on his pillow and lie there with an odd expression on his face . 

 " I never have a secret , " he say , " except that one about not live to grow up . they do not   know I know that , so it be a sort of secret . but I like this kind well . " 

 " if you will not   make they take you to the garden , " plead Mary , " perhaps I feel almost sure I can find out how to get in sometime . and then if the doctor want you to go out in your chair , and if you can always do what you want to do , perhaps perhaps we might find some boy who would push you , and we could go alone and it would always be a secret garden . " 

 " I should like that , " he say very slowly , his eye look dreamy . " I should like that . I should not mind fresh air in a secret garden . " 

 Mary begin to recover her breath and feel safe because the idea of keep the secret seem to please he . she feel almost sure that if she keep on talk and could make he see the garden in his mind as she have see it he would like it so much that he could not bear to think that everybody might tramp in to it when they choose . 

 " I will tell you what I think it would be like , if we could go into it , " she say . " it have be shut up so long thing have grow into a tangle perhaps . " 

 he lie quite still and listen while she go on talk about the rose which might have clamber from tree to tree and hang down about the many bird which might have build their nest there because it be so safe . and then she tell he about the robin and Ben Weatherstaff , and there be so much to tell about the robin and it be so easy and safe to talk about it that she cease to be afraid . the robin please he so much that he smile until he look almost beautiful , and at first Mary have think that he be even plain than herself , with his big eye and heavy lock of hair . 

 " I do not know bird could be like that , " he say . " but if you stay in a room you never see thing . what a lot of thing you know . I feel as if you have be inside that garden . " 

 she do not know what to say , so she do not say anything . he evidently do not expect an answer and the next moment he give she a surprise . 

 " I be go to let you look at something , " he say . " do you see that rose - color silk curtain hang on the wall over the mantel - piece ? " 

 Mary have not notice it before , but she look up and see it . it be a curtain of soft silk hang over what seem to be some picture . 

 " yes , " she answer . 

 " there be a cord hang from it , " say Colin . " go and pull it . " 

 Mary get up , much mystified , and find the cord . when she pull it the silk curtain run back on ring and when it run back it uncover a picture . it be the picture of a girl with a laugh face . she have bright hair tie up with a blue ribbon and her gay , lovely eye be exactly like Colin 's unhappy one , agate gray and look twice as big as they really be because of the black lash all round they . 

 " she be my mother , " say Colin complainingly . " I do not   see why she die . sometimes I hate she for do it . " 

 " how queer ! " say Mary . 

 " if she have live I believe I should not have be ill always , " he grumble . " I dare say I should have live , too . and my father would not have hat to look at I . I dare say I should have have a strong back . draw the curtain again . " 

 Mary do as she be tell and return to her footstool . 

 " she be much pretty than you , " she say , " but her eye be just like yours at least they be the same shape and color . why be the curtain draw over she ? " 

 he move uncomfortably . 

 " I make they do it , " he say . " sometimes I do not   like to see she look at I . she smile too much when I be ill and miserable . besides , she be mine and I do not   want everyone to see she . " there be a few moment of silence and then Mary speak . 

 " what would Mrs. Medlock do if she find out that I have be here ? " she inquire . 

 " she would do as I tell she to do , " he answer . " and I should tell she that I want you to come here and talk to I every day . I be glad you come . " 

 " so be I , " say Mary . " I will come as often as I can , but " she hesitate " I shall have to look every day for the garden door . " 

 " yes , you must , " say Colin , " and you can tell I about it afterward . " 

 he lie think a few minute , as he have do before , and then he speak again . 

 " I think you shall be a secret , too , " he say . " I will not tell they until they find out . I can always send the nurse out of the room and say that I want to be by myself . do you know Martha ? " 

 " yes , I know she very well , " say Mary . " she wait on I . " 

 he nod his head toward the outer corridor . 

 " she be the one who be asleep in the other room . the nurse go away yesterday to stay all night with her sister and she always make Martha attend to I when she want to go out . Martha shall tell you when to come here . " 

 then Mary understand Martha 's troubled look when she have ask question about the crying . 

 " Martha know about you all the time ? " she say . 

 " yes ; she often attend to I . the nurse like to get away from I and then Martha come . " 

 " I have be here a long time , " say Mary . " shall I go away now ? your eye look sleepy . " 

 " I wish I could go to sleep before you leave I , " he say rather shyly . 

 " shut your eye , " say Mary , draw her footstool close , " and I will do what my Ayah use to do in India . I will pat your hand and stroke it and sing something quite low . " 

 " I should like that perhaps , " he say drowsily . 

 somehow she be sorry for he and do not want he to lie awake , so she lean against the bed and begin to stroke and pat his hand and sing a very low little chant song in Hindustani . 

 " that be nice , " he say more drowsily still , and she go on chant and stroking , but when she look at he again his black lash be lie close against his cheek , for his eye be shut and he be fast asleep . so she get up softly , take her candle and creep away without make a sound . 




 CHAPTER XIV 

 a young rajah 

 the moor be hide in mist when the morning come , and the rain have not stop pour down . there could be no go out of door . Martha be so busy that Mary have no opportunity of talk to she , but in the afternoon she ask she to come and sit with she in the nursery . she come bring the stocking she be always knit when she be do nothing else . 

 " what be the matter with thee ? " she ask as soon as they sit down . " Tha ' look as if tha'd something to say . " 

 " I have . I have find out what the crying be , " say Mary . 

 Martha let she knitting drop on her knee and gaze at she with startled eye . 

 " Tha ' have not ! " she exclaim . " never ! " 

 " I hear it in the night , " Mary go on . " and I get up and go to see where it come from . it be Colin . I find he . " 

 Martha 's face become red with fright . 

 " eh ! Miss Mary ! " she say half cry . " Tha ' should not   have do it tha ' should not ! Tha'll get I in trouble . I never tell thee nothing about he but tha'll get I in trouble . I shall lose my place and what will mother do ! " 

 " you will not   lose your place , " say Mary . " he be glad I come . we talk and talk and he say he be glad I come . " 

 " be he ? " cry Martha . " art tha ' sure ? Tha ' do not   know what he be like when anything vex he . he be a big lad to cry like a baby , but when he be in a passion he will fair scream just to frighten we . he know we dare not   call our soul our own . " 

 " he be not   vex , " say Mary . " I ask he if I should go away and he make I stay . he ask I question and I sit on a big footstool and talk to he about India and about the robin and garden . he would not   let I go . he let I see his mother 's picture . before I leave he I sing he to sleep . " 

 Martha fairly gasp with amazement . 

 " I can scarcely believe thee ! " she protest . " it be as if tha'd walk straight into a lion 's den . if he have be like he be most time he would have throw himself into one of his tantrum and rouse th ' house . he will not   let stranger look at he . " 

 " he let I look at he . I look at he all the time and he look at I . we star ! " say Mary . 

 " I do not   know what to do ! " cry agitated Martha . " if Mrs. Medlock find out , she will think I break order and tell thee and I shall be pack back to mother . " 

 " he be not go to tell Mrs. Medlock anything about it yet . it be to be a sort of secret just at first , " say Mary firmly . " and he say everybody be oblige to do as he please . " 

 " Aye , that be true enough th ' bad lad ! " sigh Martha , wipe her forehead with her apron . 

 " he say Mrs. Medlock must . and he want I to come and talk to he every day . and you be to tell I when he want I . " 

 " I ! " say Martha ; " I shall lose my place I shall for sure ! " 

 " you can not   if you be do what he want you to do and everybody be order to obey he , " Mary argue . 

 " do tha ' mean to say , " cry Martha with wide open eye , " that he be nice to thee ! " 

 " I think he almost like I , " Mary answer . 

 " then tha ' must have bewitch he ! " decide Martha , draw a long breath . 

 " do you mean Magic ? " inquire Mary . " I have   hear about Magic in India , but I can not   make it . I just go into his room and I be so surprised to see he I stand and star . and then he turn round and star at I . and he think I be a ghost or a dream and I think perhaps he be . and it be so queer be there alone together in the middle of the night and not know about each other . and we begin to ask each other question . and when I ask he if I must go away he say I must not . " 

 " Th ' world 's comin ' to a end ! " gasp Martha . 

 " what be the matter with he ? " ask Mary . 

 " nobody know for sure and certain , " say Martha . " Mr. Craven go off his head like when he be bear . Th ' doctor think he would have to be put in a ' sylum . it be because Mrs. Craven die like I tell you . he would not   set eye on th ' baby . he just rave and say it would be another hunchback like he and it would well die . " 

 " be Colin a hunchback ? " Mary ask . " he do not   look like one . " 

 " he be not   yet , " say Martha . " but he begin all wrong . Mother say that there be enough trouble and rag in th ' house to set any child wrong . they be afraid his back be weak an ' they have   always be takin ' care of it keepin ' him lyin ' down and not lettin ' he walk . once they make he wear a brace but he fret so he be downright ill . then a big doctor come to see he an ' make they take it off . he talk to th ' other doctor quite rough in a polite way . he say there would be too much medicine and too much lettin ' he have his own way . " 

 " I think he be a very spoiled boy , " say Mary . 

 " he be th ' bad young nowt as ever be ! " say Martha . " I will not   say as he have not   be ill a good bit . he be have cough an ' cold that be nearly kill he two or three time . once he have rheumatic fever an ' once he have typhoid . eh ! Mrs. Medlock do get a fright then . he have be out of his head an ' she be talkin ' to th ' nurse , thinkin ' he do not   know nothing , an ' she say , ' he will die this time sure enough , an ' good thing for he an ' for everybody . ' an ' she look at he an ' there he be with his big eye open , starin ' at she as sensible as she be herself . she do not   know wha'd happen but he just star at she an ' say , ' you give I some water an ' stop talkin ' . ' " 

 " do you think he will die ? " ask Mary . 

 " mother say there be no reason why any child should live that get no fresh air an ' do not   do nothing but lie on his back an ' read picture - book an ' take medicine . he be weak and hat th ' trouble o ' bein ' take out o ' door , an ' he get cold so easy he say it make he ill . " 

 Mary sit and look at the fire . " I wonder , " she say slowly , " if it would not do he good to go out into a garden and watch thing grow . it do I good . " 

 " one of th ' bad fit he ever have , " say Martha , " be one time they take he out where the rose be by the fountain . he have be readin ' in a paper about people gettin ' something he call ' rise cold ' an ' he begin to sneeze an ' say he would got it an ' then a new gardener as do not   know th ' rule pass by an ' look at he curious . he throw himself into a passion an ' he say he have look at he because he be go to be a hunchback . he cry himself into a fever an ' be ill all night . " 

 " if he ever get angry at I , I will never go and see he again , " say Mary . 

 " he will have thee if he want thee , " say Martha . " Tha ' may as well know that at th ' start . " 

 very soon afterward a bell rang and she roll up her knitting . 

 " I dare say th ' nurse want I to stay with he a bit , " she say . " I hope he be in a good temper . " 

 she be out of the room about ten minute and then she come back with a puzzled expression . 

 " well , tha ' have bewitch he , " she say . " he be up on his sofa with his picture - book . he be tell the nurse to stay away until six o'clock . I be to wait in the next room . Th ' minute she be go he call I to he an ' say , ' I want Mary Lennox to come and talk to I , and remember you be not to tell any one . ' you would well go as quick as you can . " 

 Mary be quite willing to go quickly . she do not want to see Colin as much as she want to see Dickon ; but she want to see he very much . 

 there be a bright fire on the hearth when she enter his room , and in the daylight she see it be a very beautiful room indeed . there be rich color in the rug and hanging and picture and book on the wall which make it look glow and comfortable even in spite of the gray sky and fall rain . Colin look rather like a picture himself . he be wrap in a velvet dressing - gown and sit against a big brocade cushion . he have a red spot on each cheek . 

 " come in , " he say . " I have   be think about you all morning . " 

 " I have   be think about you , too , " answer Mary . " you do not   know how frightened Martha be . she say Mrs. Medlock will think she tell I about you and then she will be send away . " 

 he frown . 

 " go and tell she to come here , " he say . " she be in the next room . " 

 Mary go and bring she back . poor Martha be shake in her shoe . Colin be still frown . 

 " have you to do what I please or have you not ? " he demand . 

 " I have to do what you please , sir , " Martha falter , turn quite red . 

 " have Medlock to do what I please ? " 

 " everybody have , sir , " say Martha . 

 " well , then , if I order you to bring Miss Mary to I , how can Medlock send you away if she find it out ? " 

 " please do not   let she , sir , " plead Martha . 

 " I will send she away if she dare to say a word about such a thing , " say Master Craven grandly . " she would not   like that , I can tell you . " 

 " thank you , sir , " bob a curtsy , " I want to do my duty , sir . " 

 " what I want be your duty " say Colin more grandly still . " I will take care of you . now go away . " 

 when the door close behind Martha , Colin find Mistress Mary gaze at he as if he have set she wonder . 

 " why do you look at I like that ? " he ask she . " what be you think about ? " 

 " I be think about two thing . " 

 " what be they ? sit down and tell I . " 

 " this be the first one , " say Mary , seat herself on the big stool . " once in India I see a boy who be a Rajah . he have ruby and emerald and diamond stick all over he . he speak to his people just as you speak to Martha . everybody have to do everything he tell they in a minute . I think they would have be kill if they have not . " 

 " I shall make you tell I about Rajahs presently , " he say , " but first tell I what the second thing be . " 

 " I be think , " say Mary , " how different you be from Dickon . " 

 " who be Dickon ? " he say . " what a queer name ! " 

 she might as well tell he , she think she could talk about Dickon without mention the secret garden . she have like to hear Martha talk about he . besides , she long to talk about he . it would seem to bring he nearer . 

 " he be Martha 's brother . he be twelve year old , " she explain . " he be not like any one else in the world . he can charm fox and squirrel and bird just as the native in India charm snake . he play a very soft tune on a pipe and they come and listen . " 

 there be some big book on a table at his side and he drag one suddenly toward he . " there be a picture of a snake - charmer in this , " he exclaim . " come and look at it . " 

 the book be a beautiful one with superb color illustration and he turn to one of they . 

 " can he do that ? " he ask eagerly . 

 " he play on his pipe and they listen , " Mary explain . " but he do not   call it magic . he say it be because he live on the moor so much and he know their way . he say he feel sometimes as if he be a bird or a rabbit himself , he like they so . I think he ask the robin question . it seem as if they talk to each other in soft chirp . " 

 Colin lie back on his cushion and his eye grow large and large and the spot on his cheek burn . 

 " tell I some more about he , " he say . 

 " he know all about egg and nest , " Mary go on . " and he know where fox and badger and otter live . he keep they secret so that other boy will not   find their hole and frighten they . he know about everything that grow or live on the moor . " 

 " do he like the moor ? " say Colin . " how can he when it be such a great , bare , dreary place ? " 

 " it be the most beautiful place , " protest Mary . " thousand of lovely thing grow on it and there be thousand of little creature all busy building nest and make hole and burrow and chippere or singing or squeaking to each other . they be so busy and have such fun under the earth or in the tree or heather . it be their world . " 

 " how do you know all that ? " say Colin , turn on his elbow to look at she . 

 " I have never be there once , really , " say Mary suddenly remember . " I only drive over it in the dark . I think it be hideous . Martha tell I about it first and then Dickon . when Dickon talk about it you feel as if you see thing and hear they and as if you be stand in the heather with the sun shin and the gorse smelling like honey and all full of bee and butterfly . " 

 " you never see anything if you be ill , " say Colin restlessly . he look like a person listen to a new sound in the distance and wonder what it be . 

 " you can not   if you stay in a room , " say Mary . 

 " I could not   go on the moor , " he say in a resentful tone . 

 Mary be silent for a minute and then she say something bold . 

 " you might sometime . " 

 he move as if he be startle . 

 " go on the moor ! how could I ? I be go to die . " " how do you know ? " say Mary unsympathetically . she do not   like the way he have of talk about die . she do not feel very sympathetic . she feel rather as if he almost boast about it . 

 " oh , I have   hear it ever since I remember , " he answer crossly . " they be always whisper about it and think I do not   notice . they wish I would , too . " 

 Mistress Mary feel quite contrary . she pinch her lip together . 

 " if they wish I would , " she say , " I would not . who wish you would ? " 

 " the servant and of course Dr. Craven because he would get Misselthwaite and be rich instead of poor . he dare not   say so , but he always look cheerful when I be bad . when I have typhoid fever his face get quite fat . I think my father wish it , too . " 

 " I do not   believe he do , " say Mary quite obstinately . 

 that make Colin turn and look at she again . 

 " do not   you ? " he say . 

 and then he lie back on his cushion and be still , as if he be think . and there be quite a long silence . perhaps they be both of they think strange thing child do not usually think . " I like the grand doctor from London , because he make they take the iron thing off , " say Mary at last " do he say you be go to die ? " 

 " no . " . 

 " what do he say ? " 

 " he do not   whisper , " Colin answer . " perhaps he know I hat whispering . I hear he say one thing quite aloud . he say , ' the lad might live if he would make up his mind to it . put he in the humor . ' it sound as if he be in a temper . " 

 " I will tell you who would put you in the humor , perhaps , " say Mary reflect . she feel as if she would like this thing to be settle one way or the other . " I believe Dickon would . he be always talk about live thing . he never talk about dead thing or thing that be ill . he be always look up in the sky to watch bird fly or look down at the earth to see something grow . he have such round blue eye and they be so wide open with look about . and he laugh such a big laugh with his wide mouth and his cheek be as red as red as cherry . " she pull her stool nearer to the sofa and her expression quite change at the remembrance of the wide curve mouth and wide open eye . 

 " see here , " she say . " do not   let we talk about die ; I do not   like it . let we talk about living . let we talk and talk about Dickon . and then we will look at your picture . " 

 it be the good thing she could have say . to talk about Dickon mean to talk about the moor and about the cottage and the fourteen people who live in it on sixteen shilling a week and the child who get fat on the moor grass like the wild pony . and about Dickon 's mother and the skip - rope and the moor with the sun on it and about pale green point stick up out of the black sod . and it be all so alive that Mary talk more than she have ever talk before and Colin both talk and listen as he have never do either before . and they both begin to laugh over nothing as child will when they be happy together . and they laugh so that in the end they be make as much noise as if they have be two ordinary healthy natural ten - year - old creature instead of a hard , little , unlove girl and a sickly boy who believe that he be go to die . 

 they enjoy themselves so much that they forget the picture and they forget about the time . they have be laugh quite loudly over Ben Weatherstaff and his robin , and Colin be actually sit up as if he have forget about his weak back , when he suddenly remember something . " do you know there be one thing we have never once think of , " he say . " we be cousin . " 

 it seem so queer that they have talk so much and never remember this simple thing that they laugh more than ever , because they have get into the humor to laugh at anything . and in the midst of the fun the door open and in walk Dr. Craven and Mrs. Medlock . 

 Dr. Craven start in actual alarm and Mrs. Medlock almost fall back because he have accidentally bump against she . 

 " Good Lord ! " exclaim poor Mrs. Medlock with her eye almost start out of her head . " Good Lord ! " 

 " what be this ? " say Dr. Craven , come forward . " what do it mean ? " 

 then Mary be remind of the boy Rajah again . Colin answer as if neither the doctor 's alarm nor Mrs. Medlock 's terror be of the slight consequence . he be as little disturbed or frighten as if an elderly cat and dog have walk into the room . 

 " this be my cousin , Mary Lennox , " he say . " I ask she to come and talk to I . I like she . she must come and talk to I whenever I send for she . " 

 Dr. Craven turn reproachfully to Mrs. Medlock . " oh , sir " she pant . " I do not   know how it be happen . there be not a servant on the place tha'd dare to talk they all have their order . " 

 " nobody tell she anything , " say Colin . " she hear I cry and find I herself . I be glad she come . do not   be silly , Medlock . " 

 Mary see that Dr. Craven do not look pleased , but it be quite plain that he dare not oppose his patient . he sit down by Colin and feel his pulse . 

 " I be afraid there have be too much excitement . Excitement be not good for you , my boy , " he say . 

 " I should be excited if she keep away , " answer Colin , his eye begin to look dangerously sparkling . " I be well . she make I well . the nurse must bring up her tea with mine . we will have tea together . " 

 Mrs. Medlock and Dr. Craven look at each other in a troubled way , but there be evidently nothing to be do . 

 " he do look rather well , sir , " venture Mrs. Medlock . " but " think the matter over " he look well this morning before she come into the room . " 

 " she come into the room last night . she stay with I a long time . she sing a Hindustani song to I and it make I go to sleep , " say Colin . " I be well when I waken up . I want my breakfast . I want my tea now . tell nurse , Medlock . " 

 Dr. Craven do not stay very long . he talk to the nurse for a few minute when she come into the room and say a few word of warn to Colin . he must not talk too much ; he must not forget that he be ill ; he must not forget that he be very easily tired . Mary think that there seem to be a number of uncomfortable thing he be not to forget . 

 Colin look fretful and keep his strange black - lash eye fix on Dr. Craven 's face . 

 " I want to forget it , " he say at last . " she make I forget it . that be why I want she . " 

 Dr. Craven do not look happy when he leave the room . he give a puzzled glance at the little girl sit on the large stool . she have become a stiff , silent child again as soon as he enter and he could not see what the attraction be . the boy actually do look brighter , however and he sigh rather heavily as he go down the corridor . 

 " they be always want I to eat thing when I do not   want to , " say Colin , as the nurse bring in the tea and put it on the table by the sofa . " now , if you will eat I will . those muffin look so nice and hot . tell I about Rajahs . " 




 CHAPTER XV 

 NEST BUILDING 

 after another week of rain the high arch of blue sky appear again and the sun which pour down be quite hot . though there have be no chance to see either the secret garden or Dickon , Mistress Mary have enjoy herself very much . the week have not seem long . she have spend hour of every day with Colin in his room , talk about Rajahs or garden or Dickon and the cottage on the moor . they have look at the splendid book and picture and sometimes Mary have read thing to Colin , and sometimes he have read a little to she . when he be amuse and interested she think he scarcely look like an invalid at all , except that his face be so colorless and he be always on the sofa . 

 " you be a sly young one to listen and get out of your bed to go follow thing up like you do that night , " Mrs. Medlock say once . " but there be no saying it be not be a sort of blessing to the lot of we . he be not have a tantrum or a whining fit since you make friend . the nurse be just go to give up the case because she be so sick of he , but she say she do not   mind stay now you have   go on duty with she , " laugh a little . 

 in her talk with Colin , Mary have try to be very cautious about the secret garden . there be certain thing she want to find out from he , but she feel that she must find they out without ask he direct question . in the first place , as she begin to like to be with he , she want to discover whether he be the kind of boy you could tell a secret to . he be not in the least like Dickon , but he be evidently so pleased with the idea of a garden no one know anything about that she think perhaps he could be trust . but she have not know he long enough to be sure . the second thing she want to find out be this : if he could be trust if he really could would not   it be possible to take he to the garden without have any one find it out ? the grand doctor have say that he must have fresh air and Colin have say that he would not mind fresh air in a secret garden . perhaps if he have a great deal of fresh air and know Dickon and the robin and see thing grow he might not think so much about die . Mary have see herself in the glass sometimes lately when she have realize that she look quite a different creature from the child she have see when she arrive from India . this child look nicer . even Martha have see a change in she . 

 " Th ' air from th ' moor have do thee good already , " she have say . " Tha'rt not nigh so yeller and tha'rt not nigh so scrawny . even tha ' hair do not   slamp down on tha ' head so flat . it be get some life in it so as it stick out a bit . " 

 " it be like I , " say Mary . " it be grow strong and fat . I be sure there be more of it . " 

 " it look it , for sure , " say Martha , ruffle it up a little round her face . " Tha'rt not half so ugly when it be that way an ' there be a bit o ' red in tha ' cheek . " 

 if garden and fresh air have be good for she perhaps they would be good for Colin . but then , if he hat people to look at he , perhaps he would not like to see Dickon . 

 " why do it make you angry when you be look at ? " she inquire one day . 

 " I always hat it , " he answer , " even when I be very little . then when they take I to the seaside and I use to lie in my carriage everybody use to stare and lady would stop and talk to my nurse and then they would begin to whisper and I know then they be say I should not   live to grow up . then sometimes the lady would pat my cheek and say ' poor child ! ' once when a lady do that I scream out loud and bit her hand . she be so frightened she run away . " 

 " she think you have go mad like a dog , " say Mary , not at all admiringly . 

 " I do not   care what she think , " say Colin , frown . 

 " I wonder why you do not   scream and bite I when I come into your room ? " say Mary . then she begin to smile slowly . 

 " I think you be a ghost or a dream , " he say . " you can not   bite a ghost or a dream , and if you scream they do not   care . " 

 " would you hate it if if a boy look at you ? " Mary ask uncertainly . 

 he lie back on his cushion and pause thoughtfully . 

 " there be one boy , " he say quite slowly , as if he be think over every word , " there be one boy I believe I should not   mind . it be that boy who know where the fox live Dickon . " 

 " I be sure you would not   mind he , " say Mary . 

 " the bird do not   and other animal , " he say , still think it over , " perhaps that be why I should not . he be a sort of animal charmer and I be a boy animal . " 

 then he laugh and she laugh too ; in fact it end in their both laugh a great deal and find the idea of a boy animal hiding in his hole very funny indeed . 

 what Mary feel afterward be that she need not fear about Dickon . 


 on that first morning when the sky be blue again Mary waken very early . the sun be pour in slant ray through the blind and there be something so joyous in the sight of it that she jump out of bed and run to the window . she draw up the blind and open the window itself and a great waft of fresh , scented air blow in upon she . the moor be blue and the whole world look as if something Magic have happen to it . there be tender little fluting sound here and there and everywhere , as if score of bird be begin to tune up for a concert . Mary put her hand out of the window and hold it in the sun . 

 " it be warm warm ! " she say . " it will make the green point push up and up and up , and it will make the bulb and root work and struggle with all their might under the earth . " 

 she kneel down and lean out of the window as far as she could , breathe big breath and sniff the air until she laugh because she remember what Dickon 's mother have say about the end of his nose quiver like a rabbit 's . " it must be very early , " she say . " the little cloud be all pink and I have   never see the sky look like this . no one be up . I do not   even hear the stable boy . " 

 a sudden thought make she scramble to her foot . 

 " I can not   wait ! I be go to see the garden ! " 

 she have learn to dress herself by this time and she put on her clothe in five minute . she know a small side door which she could unbolt herself and she fly downstairs in her stocking foot and put on her shoe in the hall . she unchain and unbolted and unlocked and when the door be open she spring across the step with one bind , and there she be stand on the grass , which seem to have turn green , and with the sun pour down on she and warm sweet waft about she and the fluting and twitter and singing come from every bush and tree . she clasp her hand for pure joy and look up in the sky and it be so blue and pink and pearly and white and flood with springtime light that she feel as if she must flute and sing aloud herself and know that thrush and robin and skylark could not possibly help it . she run around the shrub and path towards the secret garden . 

 " it be all different already , " she say . " the grass be green and thing be stick up everywhere and thing be uncurling and green bud of leaf be show . this afternoon I be sure Dickon will come . " 

 the long warm rain have do strange thing to the herbaceous bed which border the walk by the low wall . there be thing sprout and push out from the root of clump of plant and there be actually here and there glimpse of royal purple and yellow unfurling among the stem of crocus . six month before Mistress Mary would not have see how the world be wake up , but now she miss nothing . 

 when she have reach the place where the door hide itself under the ivy , she be startle by a curious loud sound . it be the caw caw of a crow and it come from the top of the wall , and when she look up , there sit a big glossy - plumage blue - black bird , look down at she very wisely indeed . she have never see a crow so close before and he make she a little nervous , but the next moment he spread his wing and flap away across the garden . she hop he be not go to stay inside and she push the door open wonder if he would . when she get fairly into the garden she see that he probably do intend to stay because he have alight on a dwarf apple - tree and under the apple - tree be lie a little reddish animal with a bushy tail , and both of they be watch the stoop body and rust - red head of Dickon , who be kneel on the grass work hard . 

 Mary fly across the grass to he . 

 " oh , Dickon ! Dickon ! " she cry out . " how could you get here so early ! how could you ! the sun have only just get up ! " 

 he get up himself , laugh and glowing , and tousle ; his eye like a bit of the sky . 

 " eh ! " he say . " I be up long before he . how could I have stay abe ! th ' world 's all fair begin again this mornin ' , it have . an ' it be workin ' an ' hummin ' an ' scratchin ' an ' pipin ' an ' nest - buildin ' an ' breathin ' out scent , till you have   get to be out on it ' stead o ' lyin ' on your back . when th ' sun do jump up , th ' moor go mad for joy , an ' I be in the midst of th ' heather , an ' I run like mad myself , shoutin ' an ' singin ' . an ' I come straight here . I could not   have stay away . why , th ' garden be lyin ' here waitin ' ! " 

 Mary put her hand on her chest , pant , as if she have be run herself . 

 " oh , Dickon ! Dickon ! " she say . " I be so happy I can scarcely breathe ! " 

 see he talk to a stranger , the little bushy - tail animal rise from its place under the tree and come to he , and the rook , caw once , fly down from its branch and settle quietly on his shoulder . 

 " this be th ' little fox cub , " he say , rub the little reddish animal 's head . " it be name Captain . an ' this here 's soot . soot he fly across th ' moor with I an ' Captain he run same as if th ' hound have be after he . they both feel same as I do . " 

 neither of the creature look as if he be the least afraid of Mary . when Dickon begin to walk about , Soot stay on his shoulder and Captain trot quietly close to his side . 

 " see here ! " say Dickon . " see how these have push up , an ' these an ' these ! an ' eh ! look at these here ! " 

 he throw himself upon his knee and Mary go down beside he . they have come upon a whole clump of crocus burst into purple and orange and gold . Mary bend her face down and kiss and kiss they . 

 " you never kiss a person in that way , " she say when she lift her head . " flower be so different . " 

 he look puzzled but smile . 

 " eh ! " he say , " I have   kiss mother many a time that way when I come in from th ' moor after a day 's roamin ' an ' she stand there at th ' door in th ' sun , lookin ' so glad an ' comfortable . " they run from one part of the garden to another and find so many wonder that they be oblige to remind themselves that they must whisper or speak low . he show her swell leafbud on rose branch which have seem dead . he show she ten thousand new green point push through the mould . they put their eager young nose close to the earth and sniff its warm springtime breathing ; they dig and pull and laugh low with rapture until Mistress Mary 's hair be as tumble as Dickon 's and her cheek be almost as poppy red as his . 

 there be every joy on earth in the secret garden that morning , and in the midst of they come a delight more delightful than all , because it be more wonderful . swiftly something fly across the wall and dart through the tree to a close grow corner , a little flare of red - breast bird with something hang from its beak . Dickon stand quite still and put his hand on Mary almost as if they have suddenly find themselves laugh in a church . 

 " we munnot stir , " he whisper in broad Yorkshire . " we munnot scarce breathe . I know he be mate - huntin ' when I seed he last . it be Ben Weatherstaff 's robin . he be buildin ' his nest . he will stay here if we do not   fight he . " they settle down softly upon the grass and sit there without move . 

 " we must not   seem as if we be watchin ' he too close , " say Dickon . " he would be out with we for good if he get th ' notion we be interferin ' now . he will be a good bit different till all this be over . he be settin ' up housekeepin ' . he will be shyer an ' readier to take thing ill . he be get no time for visitin ' an ' gossipin ' . we must keep still a bit an ' try to look as if we be grass an ' tree an ' bush . then when he be get use to seein ' us I will chirp a bit an ' he will know us'll not be in his way . " 

 Mistress Mary be not at all sure that she know , as Dickon seem to , how to try to look like grass and tree and bush . but he have say the queer thing as if it be the simple and most natural thing in the world , and she feel it must be quite easy to he , and indeed she watch he for a few minute carefully , wonder if it be possible for he to quietly turn green and put out branch and leaf . but he only sit wonderfully still , and when he speak drop his voice to such a softness that it be curious that she could hear he , but she could . 

 " it be part o ' th ' springtime , this nest - buildin ' be , " he say . " I warrant it be be go on in th ' same way every year since th ' world be begin . they have   get their way o ' thinkin ' and do thing an ' a body have well not meddle . you can lose a friend in springtime easy than any other season if you be too curious . " 

 " if we talk about he I can not   help look at he , " Mary say as softly as possible . " we must talk of something else . there be something I want to tell you . " 

 " he will like it well if we talk o ' something else , " say Dickon . " what be it tha 's get to tell I ? " 

 " well do you know about Colin ? " she whisper . 

 he turn his head to look at she . 

 " what do tha ' know about he ? " he ask . 

 " I have   see he . I have be to talk to he every day this week . he want I to come . he say I be make he forget about be ill and die , " answer Mary . 

 Dickon look actually relieve as soon as the surprise die away from his round face . 

 " I be glad o ' that , " he exclaim . " I be right down glad . it make I easy . I know I must say nothing about he an ' I do not   like havin' to hide thing . " 

 " do not   you like hide the garden ? " say Mary . 

 " I will never tell about it , " he answer . " but I say to mother , ' mother , ' I say , ' I get a secret to keep . it be not a bad ' un , tha ' know that . it be no bad than hidin ' where a bird 's nest be . Tha ' do not   mind it , do tha ' ? ' " 

 Mary always want to hear about mother . 

 " what do she say ? " she ask , not at all afraid to hear . 

 Dickon grin sweet - temperedly . 

 " it be just like she , what she say , " he answer . " she give my head a bit of a rub an ' laugh an ' she say , ' eh , lad , tha ' can have all th ' secret tha ' like . I have   know thee twelve year ' . ' " 

 " how do you know about Colin ? " ask Mary . 

 " everybody as know about Mester Craven know there be a little lad as be like to be a cripple , an ' they know Mester Craven do not   like he to be talk about . folk be sorry for Mester Craven because Mrs. Craven be such a pretty young lady an ' they be so fond of each other . Mrs. Medlock stop in our cottage whenever she go to Thwaite an ' she do not   mind talkin ' to mother before we child , because she know we have be bring up to be trusty . how do tha ' find out about he ? Martha be in fine trouble th ' last time she come home . she say tha'd hear he frettin ' an ' tha ' be askin ' question an ' she do not   know what to say . " 

 Mary tell he her story about the midnight wuthere of the wind which have waken she and about the faint far - off sound of the complain voice which have lead she down the dark corridor with her candle and have end with her opening of the door of the dimly light room with the carven four - post bed in the corner . when she describe the small ivory - white face and the strange black - rim eye Dickon shake his head . 

 " they be just like his mother 's eye , only her be always laughin ' , they say , " he say . " they say as Mr. Craven can not   bear to see he when he be awake an ' it be because his eye be so like his mother 's an ' yet look so different in his miserable bit of a face . " 

 " do you think he want to die ? " whisper Mary . 

 " no , but he wish he would never be bear . Mother she say that be th ' bad thing on earth for a child . they as be not want scarce ever thrive . Mester Craven he would buy anythin ' as money could buy for th ' poor lad but he would like to forget as he be on earth . for one thing , he be afraid he will look at he some day and find he be grow hunchback . " 

 " Colin 's so afraid of it himself that he will not   sit up , " say Mary . " he say he be always think that if he should feel a lump come he should go crazy and scream himself to death . " 

 " eh ! he ought not   to lie there thinkin ' thing like that , " say Dickon . " no lad could get well as think they sort o ' thing . " 

 the fox be lie on the grass close by he , look up to ask for a pat now and then , and Dickon bend down and rub his neck softly and think a few minute in silence . presently he lift his head and look round the garden . 

 " when first we get in here , " he say , " it seem like everything be gray . look round now and tell I if tha ' do not   see a difference . " 

 Mary look and catch her breath a little . 

 " why ! " she cry , " the gray wall be change . it be as if a green mist be creep over it . it be almost like a green gauze veil . " 

 " aye , " say Dickon . " an ' it will be green and greener till th ' gray 's all go . can tha ' guess what I be thinkin ' ? " 

 " I know it be something nice , " say Mary eagerly . " I believe it be something about Colin . " 

 " I be thinkin ' that if he be out here he would not   be watchin ' for lump to grow on his back ; he would be watchin ' for bud to break on th ' rose - bush , an ' he would likely be healthy , " explain Dickon . " I be wonderin ' if we could ever get he in th ' humor to come out here an ' lie under th ' tree in his carriage . " 

 " I have   be wonder that myself . I have   think of it almost every time I have   talk to he , " say Mary . " I have   wonder if he could keep a secret and I have   wonder if we could bring he here without any one see we . I think perhaps you could push his carriage . the doctor say he must have fresh air and if he want we to take he out no one dare disobey he . he will not   go out for other people and perhaps they will be glad if he will go out with we . he could order the gardener to keep away so they would not   find out . " 

 Dickon be think very hard as he scratch Captain 's back . 

 " it would be good for he , I will warrant , " he say . " Us'd not be thinkin ' he would well never be bear . Us'd be just two child watchin ' a garden grow , an ' he would be another . two lad an ' a little lass just lookin ' on at th ' springtime . I warrant it would be well than doctor 's stuff . " 

 " he be be lie in his room so long and he be always be so afraid of his back that it have make he queer , " say Mary . " he know a good many thing out of book but he do not   know anything else . he say he have be too ill to notice thing and he hat go out of door and hat garden and gardener . but he like to hear about this garden because it be a secret . I dare not   tell he much but he say he want to see it . " 

 " Us'll have he out here sometime for sure , " say Dickon . " I could push his carriage well enough . have tha ' notice how th ' robin an ' his mate have be workin ' while we have   be sittin ' here ? look at he perch on that branch wonderin ' where it would be good to put that twig he be get in his beak . " 

 he make one of his low whistle call and the robin turn his head and look at he inquiringly , still hold his twig . Dickon speak to he as Ben Weatherstaff do , but Dickon 's tone be one of friendly advice . 

 " wheres'ever tha ' put it , " he say , " it will be all right . Tha ' know how to build tha ' nest before tha ' come out o ' th ' egg . get on with thee , lad . Tha'st get no time to lose . " 

 " oh , I do like to hear you talk to he ! " Mary say , laugh delightedly . " Ben Weatherstaff scold he and make fun of he , and he hop about and look as if he understand every word , and I know he like it . Ben Weatherstaff say he be so conceited he would rather have stone throw at he than not be notice . " 

 Dickon laugh too and go on talk . 

 " Tha ' know we will not   trouble thee , " he say to the robin . " Us be near bein ' wild thing ourselves . Us be nest - buildin ' too , bless thee . look out tha ' do not   tell on we . " 

 and though the robin do not answer , because his beak be occupy , Mary know that when he fly away with his twig to his own corner of the garden the darkness of his dew - bright eye mean that he would not tell their secret for the world . 




 CHAPTER XVI 

 " I won't ! " say MARY 

 they find a great deal to do that morning and Mary be late in return to the house and be also in such a hurry to get back to her work that she quite forget Colin until the last moment . 

 " tell Colin that I can not   come and see he yet , " she say to Martha . " I be very busy in the garden . " 

 Martha look rather frightened . 

 " eh ! Miss Mary , " she say , " it may put he all out of humor when I tell he that . " 

 but Mary be not as afraid of he as other people be and she be not a self - sacrifice person . 

 " I can not   stay , " she answer . " Dickon 's wait for I ; " and she run away . 

 the afternoon be even lovely and busy than the morning have be . already nearly all the weed be clear out of the garden and most of the rose and tree have be prune or dig about . Dickon have bring a spade of his own and he have teach Mary to use all her tool , so that by this time it be plain that though the lovely wild place be not likely to become a " gardener 's garden " it would be a wilderness of grow thing before the springtime be over . 

 " there will be apple blossom an ' cherry blossom overhead , " Dickon say , work away with all his might . " an ' there will be peach an ' plum tree in bloom against th ' wall , an ' th ' grass'll be a carpet o ' flower . " 

 the little fox and the rook be as happy and busy as they be , and the robin and his mate fly backward and forward like tiny streak of lightning . sometimes the rook flap his black wing and soar away over the tree - top in the park . each time he come back and perch near Dickon and caw several time as if he be relate his adventure , and Dickon talk to he just as he have talk to the robin . once when Dickon be so busy that he do not answer he at first , Soot fly on to his shoulder and gently tweak his ear with his large beak . when Mary want to rest a little Dickon sit down with she under a tree and once he take his pipe out of his pocket and play the soft strange little note and two squirrel appear on the wall and look and listen . 

 " Tha 's a good bit strong than tha ' be , " Dickon say , look at she as she be dig . " Tha 's beginning to look different , for sure . " 

 Mary be glow with exercise and good spirit . 

 " I be get fat and fat every day , " she say quite exultantly . " Mrs. Medlock will have to get I some big dress . Martha say my hair be grow thick . it be not   so flat and stringy . " 

 the sun be begin to set and send deep gold - color ray slant under the tree when they part . 

 " it will be fine tomorrow , " say Dickon . " I will be at work by sunrise . " 

 " so will I , " say Mary . 


 she run back to the house as quickly as her foot would carry she . she want to tell Colin about Dickon 's fox cub and the rook and about what the springtime have be do . she feel sure he would like to hear . so it be not very pleasant when she open the door of her room , to see Martha standing wait for she with a doleful face . 

 " what be the matter ? " she ask . " what do Colin say when you tell he I could not   come ? " 

 " eh ! " say Martha , " I wish tha'd go . he be nigh go into one o ' his tantrum . there be be a nice to do all afternoon to keep he quiet . he would watch the clock all th ' time . " 

 Mary 's lip pinch themselves together . she be no more used to consider other people than Colin be and she see no reason why an ill - temper boy should interfere with the thing she like well . she know nothing about the pitifulness of people who have be ill and nervous and who do not know that they could control their temper and need not make other people ill and nervous , too . when she have have a headache in India she have do she good to see that everybody else also have a headache or something quite as bad . and she feel she be quite right ; but of course now she feel that Colin be quite wrong . 

 he be not on his sofa when she go into his room . he be lie flat on his back in bed and he do not turn his head toward she as she come in . this be a bad beginning and Mary march up to he with her stiff manner . 

 " why do not   you get up ? " she say . 

 " I do get up this morning when I think you be come , " he answer , without look at she . " I make they put I back in bed this afternoon . my back ache and my head ache and I be tired . why do not   you come ? " " I be work in the garden with Dickon , " say Mary . 

 Colin frown and condescend to look at she . 

 " I will not   let that boy come here if you go and stay with he instead of come to talk to I , " he say . 

 Mary fly into a fine passion . she could fly into a passion without make a noise . she just grow sour and obstinate and do not care what happen . 

 " if you send Dickon away , I will never come into this room again ! " she retort . 

 " you will have to if I want you , " say Colin . 

 " I will not ! " say Mary . 

 " I will make you , " say Colin . " they shall drag you in . " 

 " shall they , Mr. Rajah ! " say Mary fiercely . " they may drag I in but they can not   make I talk when they get I here . I will sit and clench my tooth and never tell you one thing . I will not   even look at you . I will stare at the floor ! " 

 they be a nice agreeable pair as they glare at each other . if they have be two little street boy they would have spring at each other and have a rough - and - tumble fight . as it be , they do the next thing to it . 

 " you be a selfish thing ! " cry Colin . 

 " what be you ? " say Mary . " selfish people always say that . any one be selfish who do not   do what they want . you be more selfish than I be . you be the most selfish boy I ever see . " 

 " I be not ! " snap Colin . " I be not as selfish as your fine Dickon be ! he keep you play in the dirt when he know I be all by myself . he be selfish , if you like ! " 

 Mary 's eye flash fire . 

 " he be nice than any other boy that ever live ! " she say . " he be he be like an angel ! " it might sound rather silly to say that but she do not care . 

 " a nice angel ! " Colin sneer ferociously . " he be a common cottage boy off the moor ! " 

 " he be well than a common Rajah ! " retort Mary . " he be a thousand time well ! " 

 because she be the strong of the two she be begin to get the well of he . the truth be that he have never have a fight with any one like himself in his life and , upon the whole , it be rather good for he , though neither he nor Mary know anything about that . he turn his head on his pillow and shut his eye and a big tear be squeeze out and run down his cheek . he be begin to feel pathetic and sorry for himself not for any one else . 

 " I be not as selfish as you , because I be always ill , and I be sure there be a lump come on my back , " he say . " and I be go to die besides . " 

 " you be not ! " contradict Mary unsympathetically . 

 he open his eye quite wide with indignation . he have never hear such a thing say before . he be at once furious and slightly pleased , if a person could be both at one time . 

 " I be not ? " he cry . " I be ! you know I be ! everybody say so . " 

 " I do not   believe it ! " say Mary sourly . " you just say that to make people sorry . I believe you be proud of it . I do not   believe it ! if you be a nice boy it might be true but you be too nasty ! " 

 in spite of his invalid back Colin sit up in bed in quite a healthy rage . 

 " get out of the room ! " he shout and he catch hold of his pillow and throw it at she . he be not strong enough to throw it far and it only fall at her foot , but Mary 's face look as pinch as a nutcracker . 

 " I be go , " she say . " and I will not   come back ! " she walk to the door and when she reach it she turn round and speak again . 

 " I be go to tell you all sort of nice thing , " she say . " Dickon bring his fox and his rook and I be go to tell you all about they . now I will not   tell you a single thing ! " 

 she march out of the door and close it behind she , and there to her great astonishment she find the train nurse stand as if she have be listen and , more amazing still she be laugh . she be a big handsome young woman who ought not to have be a train nurse at all , as she could not bear invalid and she be always make excuse to leave Colin to Martha or any one else who would take her place . Mary have never like she , and she simply stand and gaze up at she as she stand giggle into her handkerchief .. 

 " what be you laugh at ? " she ask she . 

 " at you two young one , " say the nurse . " it be the good thing that could happen to the sickly pamper thing to have some one to stand up to he that be as spoil as himself ; " and she laugh into her handkerchief again . " if he have have a young vixen of a sister to fight with it would have be the saving of he . " 

 " be he go to die ? " 

 " I do not   know and I do not   care , " say the nurse . " hysteric and temper be half what ail he . " 

 " what be hysteric ? " ask Mary . 

 " you will find out if you work he into a tantrum after this but at any rate you have   give he something to have hysteric about , and I be glad of it . " 

 Mary go back to her room not feel at all as she have feel when she have come in from the garden . she be cross and disappointed but not at all sorry for Colin . she have look forward to tell he a great many thing and she have mean to try to make up her mind whether it would be safe to trust he with the great secret . she have be begin to think it would be , but now she have change her mind entirely . she would never tell he and he could stay in his room and never get any fresh air and die if he like ! it would serve he right ! she feel so sour and unrelenting that for a few minute she almost forget about Dickon and the green veil creep over the world and the soft wind blow down from the moor .

 " Mr. Craven send it to you , " say Martha . " it look as if it have picture - book in it . " 

 Mary remember what he have ask she the day she have go to his room . " do you want anything doll toy book ? " she open the package wonder if he have send a doll , and also wonder what she should do with it if he have . but he have not send one . there be several beautiful book such as Colin have , and two of they be about garden and be full of picture . there be two or three game and there be a beautiful little writing - case with a gold monogram on it and a gold pen and inkstand . 

 everything be so nice that her pleasure begin to crowd her anger out of her mind . she have not expect he to remember she at all and her hard little heart grow quite warm . 

 " I can write well than I can print , " she say , " and the first thing I shall write with that pen will be a letter to tell he I be much oblige . " 

 if she have be friend with Colin she would have run to show he her present at once , and they would have look at the picture and read some of the gardening book and perhaps try play the game , and he would have enjoy himself so much he would never once have think he be go to die or have put his hand on his spine to see if there be a lump come . he have a way of do that which she could not bear . it give she an uncomfortable frightened feeling because he always look so frightened himself . he say that if he feel even quite a little lump some day he should know his hunch have begin to grow . something he have hear Mrs. Medlock whisper to the nurse have give he the idea and he have think over it in secret until it be quite firmly fix in his mind . Mrs. Medlock have say his father 's back have begin to show its crookedness in that way when he be a child . he have never tell any one but Mary that most of his " tantrum " as they call they grow out of his hysterical hide fear . Mary have be sorry for he when he have tell she . 

 " he always begin to think about it when he be cross or tired , " she say to herself . " and he have be cross today . perhaps perhaps he have be think about it all afternoon . " 

 she stand still , look down at the carpet and thinking . 

 " I say I would never go back again " she hesitate , knit her brow " but perhaps , just perhaps , I will go and see if he want I in the morning . perhaps he will try to throw his pillow at I again , but I think I will go . " 




 CHAPTER XVII 

 a TANTRUM 

 she have get up very early in the morning and have work hard in the garden and she be tired and sleepy , so as soon as Martha have bring her supper and she have eat it , she be glad to go to bed . as she lay her head on the pillow she murmur to herself : 

 " I will go out before breakfast and work with Dickon and then afterward I believe I will go to see he . " 

 she think it be the middle of the night when she be awaken by such dreadful sound that she jump out of bed in an instant . what be it what be it ? the next minute she feel quite sure she know . door be open and shut and there be hurry foot in the corridor and some one be cry and scream at the same time , scream and cry in a horrible way .

 CHAPTER XIX 

 " it have come ! " 

 of course Dr. Craven have be send for the morning after Colin have have his tantrum . he be always send for at once when such a thing occur and he always find , when he arrive , a white shaken boy lie on his bed , sulky and still so hysterical that he be ready to break into fresh sobbing at the least word . in fact , Dr. Craven dread and detest the difficulty of these visit . on this occasion he be away from Misselthwaite Manor until afternoon .

" " well , well , " he say . " if it amuse you perhaps it will not   do you any harm . do you take your bromide last night , Colin ? "

 CHAPTER XX 

 " I shall live forever and ever and ever ! "

 CHAPTER XXI 

 BEN WEATHERSTAFF 

 one of the strange thing about live in the world be that it be only now and then one be quite sure one be go to live forever and ever and ever . one know it sometimes when one get up at the tender solemn dawn - time and go out and stand alone and throw one 's head far back and look up and up and watch the pale sky slowly change and flush and marvelous unknown thing happen until the East almost make one cry out and one 's heart stand still at the strange unchanging majesty of the rise of the sun which have be happen every morning for thousand and thousand and thousand of year . one know it then for a moment or so . and one know it sometimes when one stand by oneself in a wood at sunset and the mysterious deep gold stillness slant through and under the branch seem to be say slowly again and again something one can not quite hear , however much one try . then sometimes the immense quiet of the dark blue at night with million of star wait and watch make one sure ; and sometimes a sound of far - off music make it true ; and sometimes a look in some one 's eye . 

 and it be like that with Colin when he first see and hear and feel the Springtime inside the four high wall of a hide garden . that afternoon the whole world seem to devote itself to be perfect and radiantly beautiful and kind to one boy . perhaps out of pure heavenly goodness the spring come and crown everything it possibly could into that one place . More than once Dickon pause in what he be do and stand still with a sort of grow wonder in his eye , shake his head softly . 

 " eh ! it be graidely , " he say . " I be twelve go on thirteen an ' there be a lot o ' afternoon in thirteen year , but seem to I like I never seed one as graidely as this ' ere . " 

 " Aye , it be a graidely one , " say Mary , and she sigh for mere joy . " I will warrant it be the graidel one as ever be in this world . "

 and delight reign . they draw the chair under the plum - tree , which be snow - white with blossom and musical with bee . it be like a king 's canopy , a fairy king 's . there be flower cherry - tree near and apple - tree whose bud be pink and white , and here and there one have burst open wide . between the blossoming branch of the canopy bit of blue sky look down like wonderful eye .

Dickon push the chair slowly round and round the garden , stop every other moment to let he look at wonder spring out of the earth or trail down from tree . it be like be take in state round the country of a magic king and queen and show all the mysterious rich it contain . 

 " I wonder if we shall see the robin ? " say Colin . 

 " Tha'll see he often enow after a bit , " answer Dickon . " when th ' egg hatch out th ' little chap he will be kep ' so busy it will make his head swim . Tha'll see he flyin ' backward an ' for'ard carryin ' worms nigh as big as himsel ' an ' that much noise go on in th ' nest when he get there as fair fluster he so as he scarce know which big mouth to drop th ' first piece in . an ' gapin ' beak an ' squawk on every side . Mother say as when she see th ' work a robin have to keep they gapin ' beak fill , she feel like she be a lady with nothing to do . she say she be see th ' little chap when it seem like th ' sweat must be droppin ' off them , though folk can not   see it . "

 " yes , " answer Dickon , after it , and his low voice have a very gentle sound .

 " the branch be quite gray and there be not a single leaf anywhere , " Colin go on . " it be quite dead , be not   it ? "

 " it look as if a big branch have be break off , " say Colin . " I wonder how it be do . "

 and so they be safe .

" for both she and Dickon have be afraid Colin might ask something about the tree whose branch have break off ten year ago and they have talk it over together and Dickon have stand and rub his head in a troubled way .

" an ' mother she think maybe she be about Misselthwaite many a time lookin ' after Mester Colin , same as all mother do when they be take out o ' th ' world . they have to come back , tha ' see . happen she be be in the garden an ' happen it be she set we to work , an ' tell we to bring he here .  when the SUN go down

 CHAPTER XXIII 

 MAGIC

" then something begin push thing up out of the soil and make thing out of nothing . one day thing be not   there and another they be . ' and I do . Magic be make I well ! I be go to be as strong as Dickon , as strong as Dickon ! ' and you must all do it , too . that be my experiment will you help , Ben Weatherstaff ? "

 CHAPTER XXIV 

 " LET they LAUGH "

 " yesterday , " he say one morning after an absence , " I go to Thwaite for mother an ' near th ' blue cow Inn I seed Bob Haworth . he be the strong chap on th ' moor . he be the champion wrestler an ' he can jump high than any other chap an ' throw th ' hammer far . he be go all th ' way to Scotland for th ' sport some year . he be know I ever since I be a little ' un an ' he be a friendly sort an ' I ax he some question . Th ' gentry call he a athlete and I think o ' thee , Mester Colin , and I say , ' how do tha ' make tha ' muscle stick out that way , Bob ? do tha ' do anythin ' extra to make thysel ' so strong ? ' an ' he say ' well , yes , lad , I do . a strong man in a show that come to Thwaite once show I how to exercise my arm an ' leg an ' every muscle in my body . an ' I say , ' could a delicate chap make himself strong with them , Bob ? ' an ' he laugh an ' say , ' art tha ' th ' delicate chap ? ' an ' I say , ' no , but I know a young gentleman that be gettin ' well of a long illness an ' I wish I know some o ' they trick to tell he about .
